ولاية الالزام بخلاف التصرف فى المال لانه يتكرر فلايمكن تدارک الخلل فلا تفيدا لولاية الاملزمة ومع القصور لايثبت ولاية الالزام وجه قوله فى المسالة الثانية ان الثيابة سبب لحدوث الرأى لوجود الممارسة فادرنا الحكم عليها تيسيرا ولنا ما ذكرنا من تحقق الحاجة ووفور الشفقة ولا ممارسة تحدث الراى بدون الشهوة فيد ارالحكم على الصغر ثم الذي يؤيد كلامنا فيما تقدم قوله عليه السلام النكاح الى العصبات من غير فصل والترتيب فى العصبات فى ولايته النكاح كالترتيب في الارث والابعد محجوب بالاقرب ترجمہ اور جائز ہے میرا اور صغیرہ کا نکاح جبکہ ان دونوں کا نکاح کیا ولی نے باکرہ ہو یا ثیبہ اور ولی وہ ہے جو عصبہ ہو اور امام مالک ہمارے خلاف ہیں باپ کے علاوہ میں اور امام شافعی خلاف ہیں باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ میں شیب صغیرہ میں بھی اختلاف ہے امام مالک کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ولایت آزاد عورت پر باعتبار حاجت کے ہے۔ اور کوئی حاجت نہیں شہوت کے معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے مگر یہ کہ باپ کی ولایت ثابت ہے بذریعہ نص خلاف قیاس اور دادا باپ کے معنی میں نہیں ہے۔ پس دادا کو باپ کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ ہم جواب دیں گے کہ نہیں بلکہ قیاس کے موافق ہے اسلئے کہ نکاح بہت سے مصالح کو متضمن ہے اور مصالح پورے طور پر حاصل نہیں ہو سکتے مگر دو برابر والوں کے درمیان عادۃ ۔ اور ہر زمانہ میں کفو کا ملنا بھی آسان نہیں۔ پس ہم نے ولایت کو ثابت کر دیا حالت صغر میں کفو کومحفوظ کرنے کے لئے۔ اور امام شافعی کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ شفقت پوری نہیں ہوگی باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ کی طرف سپرد کرنے سے۔ کیونکہ باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ کی شفقت ناقص اور قرابت بعید ہے اور اسی وجہ سے مالک نہیں ہو گا مال میں تصرف کا باوجود یکہ مال مرتبہ میں ادنیٰ ہے پس بدرجہ اولی مالک نہیں ہوگا۔ نفس میں تصرف کا درانحالیکہ نفس مرتبہ میں اعلیٰ ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرابت داعی الی النظر ہے جیسا کہ باپ اور دادا میں اور باپ دادا کے علاوہ میں جو کچھ قصور ہے اس کو ہم ظاہر کریں گے ولایت الزام کو سلب کر کے بخلاف تصرف فی المال کے اس لئے کہ وہ مکر رہوتا ہے پس خلل کا تدارک ممکن نہیں۔ پس نہیں فائدہ دے گی ولایت مگر الزام اور قصور شفقت کے ساتھ ولایت الزام ثابت نہیں ہوتی ۔ اور امام شافعی کے قول کی وجہ دوسرے مسئلہ میں یہ ہے کہ نیبر ہو نا سبب ہے رائے کے پیدا ہونے
It is permissible to marry a minor boy and a minor girl when they are married by the guardian, whether the girl is a virgin or non-virgin. And the guardian is the asaba. Malik differs from us regarding a guardian other than the father, and Shafi'i differs regarding other than the father and grandfather, and also regarding the non-virgin minor girl. The basis of Malik's argument: Guardianship over a free woman is based on need, and there is no need due to the absence of sexual desire. However, the father's guardianship is established by text (nass) contrary to analogy (qiyas), and the grandfather is not in the same meaning, so he is not annexed. We answer: Rather, it is in accordance with qiyas, because marriage contains many benefits, and benefits are not fully realized except between equals (kafa'ah) normally, and suitable matches are not agreed upon in every time. So we established guardianship during minority to secure a suitable match. The basis of Shafi'i's argument: Interest (nazar) cannot be achieved by entrusting to someone other than the father and grandfather due to weakness of their affection and distance of kinship. For this reason, they cannot dispose of property even though it is of a lower rank, so a fortiori they cannot dispose of the person (in marriage) which is of a higher rank. Our argument: Kinship is a motivation for caring, as in the case of the father and grandfather. And we will demonstrate the deficiency in others by negating the power of binding (wilayat al-ilzam), unlike disposing of property because it is recurrent, so rectifying defects is not possible, so only the binding guardianship is not beneficial. And with deficiency, binding guardianship is not established. The basis of his (Shafi'i's) statement in the second issue (regarding the minor non-virgin): That being a thayyib (non-virgin) is a cause for the occurrence of opinion due to experience, so we made the ruling dependent on it for facilitation. Our argument: What we mentioned of the realization of need and abundance of affection, and no experience creates opinion without desire, so the ruling depends on minority. Then what supports our statement previously is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Marriage (authority) belongs to the asaba' without distinction, and the order among asaba in the authority of marriage is like the order in inheritance: the more distant is blocked by the closer. Translation: And it is permissible to marry a minor boy and girl when they are married by the guardian, whether the girl is a virgin or non-virgin. And the guardian is the one who is an asaba. Imam Malik opposes us regarding other than the father, and Imam Shafi'i opposes regarding other than the father and grandfather, and there is also difference regarding the minor thayyib. The basis of Imam Malik's argument: Guardianship over a free woman is based on need, and there is no need due to the absence of sexual desire. However, the father's guardianship is established by text contrary to qiyas, and the grandfather is not in his meaning, so the grandfather should not be annexed to the father. We answer: No, rather it is in accordance with qiyas, because marriage contains many benefits, and benefits cannot be fully realized except between equals. And in every time, finding a suitable match is not easy. So we established guardianship during childhood to preserve a suitable match. The basis of Imam Shafi'i's argument: Affection will not be complete by entrusting to other than the father and grandfather, because affection of other than father and grandfather is deficient and their kinship is distant. For this reason, they cannot dispose of property even though property is of a lower rank, so a fortiori they cannot dispose of the person in marriage, which is of a higher rank. Our argument: Kinship is a motivation for caring, as in the father and grandfather. And we will make apparent the deficiency in others by removing the power of binding guardianship, unlike disposing of property because it is recurrent, so rectification of harm is not possible. So the binding guardianship will not be of benefit. And with deficiency, binding guardianship is not established. The basis of Imam Shafi'i's argument in the second issue: That being a thayyib is a cause for the occurrence of opinion due to experience, so we made the ruling depend on it for facilitation. Our argument: What we mentioned of the realization of need and abundance of affection, and no experience creates opinion without desire, so the ruling depends on (she being) a minor.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that all asaba (agnatic relatives) have the authority to contract marriage for minor children, and it rebuts the positions of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i. The matn states the permissibility for a guardian to marry a minor boy or girl, whether the girl is a virgin or thayyib (non-virgin), and defines the guardian as any asaba. The commentary then addresses two opposing views: Maliki limits guardianship to the father, and Shafi'i limits to father and grandfather, with additional nuance for a thayyib minor. Malik's argument rests on the absence of need due to lack of desire, and the father's authority being an exception to qiyas. The Hanafi response argues that the need is for securing a suitable match (kafaa), which is a benefit, and the grandfather is included by qiyas because the 'illa (effective cause) of need exists in him too. Shafi'i's argument that only father and grandfather have sufficient affection is countered by noting that all asaba share a caring motivation, but their deficiency appears in binding authority (wilayat al-ilzam), not in permissibility of contract; moreover, financial matters require more caution due to recurrence, so the analogy from property to marriage is flawed. For the thayyib minor, Shafi'i holds that her experience gives her the capacity to form an opinion, so her guardian cannot force her. The Hanafi response asserts that desire is absent in minors, so experience without desire does not produce valid opinion. The passage concludes with the hadith 'al-nikahu ila al-asabat' (marriage authority belongs to asaba), and the hierarchy among asaba follows the inheritance order (closer prevents farther).

Key Terms
ولی (wali): Guardian with authority to contract marriage for a minor. In Hanafi, it is the asaba relative.
عصبہ (asabah): Agnatic relatives (relatives through male line) who are legal heirs.
صغیر (saghir): Minor child who has not attained puberty.
صغیرہ (saghirah): Minor girl.
باکرہ (bikr): Virgin girl (who has not been married before).
ثیبہ (thayyib): Non-virgin girl who has been married before.
ولایت (wilayah): Legal authority to act on behalf of another, especially in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who besides the father and grandfather can contract marriage for a minor girl?
A) Only the father and grandfather.
B) Any asaba relative, such as an uncle or brother.
C) Only the mother or maternal uncle.
D) Only the judge (qadi).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the authority to marry a minor extends to all agnatic relatives (asaba), ensuring the child's marital interests are safeguarded.

Guardianship in Marriage of Minors: Hanafi Position and Ikhtilaf
Dispute on who can be wali and on whom wilaya applies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on who can be a wali for a minor in marriage, identify the Maliki and Shafi'i objections, and apply the Hanafi responses to determine the ruling in a given scenario.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, any agnatic relative can marry off a minor to secure compatibility; only father (Maliki) or father/grandfather (Shafi'i) suffice for others, and non-virgin minors are excluded by Shafi'i.

This lesson examines a key dispute in Islamic marriage law: who has the authority to contract the marriage of a minor? The Hanafi school holds that any agnatic relative (asaba) can serve as guardian, while the Maliki and Shafi'i schools limit this authority. The discussion involves proofs from analogy, hadith, and the concepts of need and compatibility. Understanding this dispute helps clarify the boundaries of guardianship and the practical consequences for family law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on wilaya for minors
Identify the ruling in the matn: marriage of a minor is valid when contracted by the wali, who is any asaba. Note that this applies to both virgin and non-virgin girls.
The wali must be an agnatic relative as per the order of inheritance.
2
Identify the Maliki objection and its basis
Malik restricts wilaya to the father only. His argument: need (haja) is absent in minors due to lack of desire, and the father's authority is established by text contrary to analogy (qiyas).
Malik does not extend this to the grandfather because he is not in the same meaning as the father.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to Malik
The Hanafi response: guardianship is actually in accordance with qiyas because marriage contains benefits (masalih) that require compatibility (kafa'a), which may be lost if delayed. Thus, early marriage secures compatibility.
This shows that the father's wilaya is not an exception but is on principle.
4
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its basis
Shafi'i restricts wilaya to father and grandfather due to deficient compassion in others, and also excludes non-virgin minors because experience (mumarasa) gives them opinion (ra'y).
Shafi'i uses the analogy of property: if a non-father cannot dispose of property (lower rank), he cannot dispose of the self (higher rank).
5
Analyze the Hanafi response to Shafi'i
The Hanafi response: kinship prompts consideration, and any deficiency is addressed by not giving binding authority (but Hanafi does give it). For non-virgin minors, experience without desire does not produce valid opinion; need remains. The hadith 'Marriage is entrusted to the agnatic relatives' supports the Hanafi position.
The Hanafi school relies on the explicit hadith and the analogy with inheritance order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز نكاح الصغير و الصغيرة اذا زوجهما الولى بكرا كانت الصغيرة اوثيبا والولى هو العصبة ومالك يخالفنافی غیر الاب والشافعى فى غير الاب والجدوفى الثيب الصغيرة ايضا وجه قول مالك ان الولاية على الحرة باعتبار الحاجة ولاحاجة لانعدام الشهوة الاان ولاية الاب ثبتت نصا بخلاف القياس والجد ليس في معناه فلايلحق به قلنا لابل هو موافق للقياس لان النكاح يتضمن المصالح ولاتتوفر الابين المتكافيين عادة و لا يتفق الكفوفي كل زمان فاثبتنا الولاية فى حالة الصغر احراز اللكفو وجه قول الشافعي ان النظر لايتم بالتفويض الى غير الاب والجد لقصور شفقته وبعد قرابة ولهذا لايملك التصرف في المال مع انه ادنى رتبة فلان لايملك التصرف فى النفس وانه اعلى اولى ولنا ان القرابة داعية الى النظر كمافي الاب والجد و ما فيه من القصور اظهر ناه فى سلب ولاية الالزام بخلاف التصرف فى المال لانه يتكرر فلا يمكن تدارک الخلل فلا تفيدا لولاية الاملزمة ومع القصور لايثبت ولاية الالزام وجه قوله فى المسالة الثانية ان الثيابة سبب لحدوث الرأى لوجود الممارسة فادرنا الحكم عليها تيسيرا ولنا ما ذكرنا من تحقق الحاجة ووفور الشفقة ولا ممارسة تحدث الراى بدون الشهوة فيد ارالحكم على الصغر ثم الذي يؤيد كلامنا فيما تقدم قوله عليه السلام النكاح الى العصبات من غير فصل والترتيب فى العصبات فى ولايته النكاح كالترتيب في الارث والابعد محجوب بالاقرب
And the marriage of a minor boy and a minor girl is permissible when their guardian marries them, whether the minor girl is a virgin or a non-virgin. The guardian is the agnatic relative. Malik differs regarding other than the father, and al-Shafi'i differs regarding other than the father and grandfather, and also regarding the non-virgin minor girl. The face of Malik's argument is that guardianship over a free woman is based on need, and there is no need due to lack of desire, except that the father's guardianship is established by text contrary to analogy, and the grandfather is not in his meaning, so he is not attached to him. We say: rather, it is in accordance with analogy, because marriage contains benefits, and they are not fully realized except between two compatible persons customarily, and compatibility is not found in every time, so we established guardianship in the state of minority to secure compatibility. The face of al-Shafi'i's argument is that consideration is not complete by entrusting to other than the father and grandfather due to the deficiency of his affection and distance of kinship; therefore, he does not possess authority over property even though it is a lower rank, so it is more appropriate that he does not possess authority over the self, which is higher. And our proof is that kinship necessitates consideration as in the case of the father and grandfather, and whatever deficiency exists, we manifest it by stripping the binding authority, contrary to authority over property because it is recurrent, so the defect cannot be remedied, so binding authority is not beneficial, and with deficiency, binding authority is not established. The face of his argument in the second issue is that being a non-virgin is a cause for the emergence of opinion due to the presence of experience, so we applied the ruling to it for facilitation. And our proof is what we mentioned of the existence of need and abundance of affection, and no experience produces an opinion without desire, so the ruling is applied to minority. Then what supports our statement in the preceding is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Marriage is entrusted to the agnatic relatives' without differentiation, and the order among agnatic relatives in guardianship of marriage is like the order in inheritance, and the more distant is blocked by the nearer.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about guardianship (wilaya) in the marriage of minors (saghir/saghira). The matn states that it is permissible for the wali (guardian) to marry a minor boy or girl, whether the girl is virgin or non-virgin. The wali is defined as the 'asaba (agnatic relative). The commentator then presents the positions of Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i who differ. Imam Malik restricts wilaya to the father only, based on need (haja): minors have no sexual desire so no need, except the father by text (nass) contrary to analogy (qiyas). The grandfather is not analogous to the father in affection. The Hanafi response is that guardianship is actually in accordance with qiyas because marriage involves multiple benefits (masalih) that require compatibility (kafa'a), which may be lost if waiting till adulthood. Thus, early marriage preserves compatibility. Imam al-Shafi'i restricts wilaya to father and grandfather, arguing that others lack complete compassion (shafaqa) and close kinship, and they lack authority over property (mal) let alone over the self (nafs). The Hanafi response is that kinship does prompt consideration, and any deficiency in compassion is addressed by not giving binding authority (wilayat al-ilzam) to non-father/grandfather guardians. However, the Hanafi school gives binding authority even to non-father/grandfather asaba because the need is established and compassion is sufficient. Regarding the second issue (whether wilaya applies to a non-virgin minor girl), al-Shafi'i says no because her experience (mumarasa) gives her opinion (ra'y), so she does not need a guardian. The Hanafi response is that need still exists, and experience without desire does not produce valid opinion, so the ruling of minority remains. The passage concludes with the hadith: 'Marriage is entrusted to the agnatic relatives' (al-nikahu ila al-'asabat) and the order among them is like inheritance, where the nearer excludes the farther. This is a dalil naqli supporting the Hanafi position that all asaba are eligible.

Key Terms
صغير (saghir): A minor child who has not reached puberty.
ولى (wali): Guardian who has authority to contract marriage for a minor. In this passage, wali is the 'asaba (agnatic relative).
عصبة (asaba): Agnatic relatives who inherit as residuaries. In marriage, they are eligible to act as guardians.
ثيب (thayyib): A non-virgin woman, one who has previously been married.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who can be a wali for the marriage of a minor girl?
A) Only her father
B) Only her father or grandfather
C) Any agnatic relative (asaba)
D) Her mother

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows any agnatic relative (asaba) to contract the marriage of a minor, based on the need for compatibility and the hadith on asaba guardianship; other schools restrict this authority to the father or father/grandfather, and also exclude non-virgin minors according to Shafi'i.

Who Holds Guardianship in Marriage? The Hanafi Position vs. Maliki and Shafi'i
Explains the first issue of the guardianship dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on who holds guardianship in marriage and explain how it differs from the Maliki and Shafi'i positions.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, every agnate holds guardianship, but only father and grandfather can make it binding.

This lesson examines the first of two central disputes in Islamic marriage law: who is authorized to act as a guardian (wali) in a marriage contract. The Hanafi school adopts a broad definition, including all agnate relatives, while the Maliki school restricts it to the father alone and the Shafi'i school to the father and grandfather. We will analyze the evidence each school presents and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds that every agnate (asabah) has guardianship (wilayah) in marriage, with the father and grandfather having additional binding authority (wilayat ilzam).
The basis is need (hajah) and affection (shafaqah) found in all agnates.
2
Identify opposing schools and their positions
State that Imam Malik restricts guardianship to the father only, and Imam al-Shafi'i extends it to the father and grandfather only.
Malik relies on a specific hadith; Shafi'i relies on analogy to property.
3
Follow the opposing proofs
Examine the Maliki proof (hadith of Abu Bakr marrying his minor daughter) and the Shafi'i proof (analogy to guardianship over property and the assumption of strongest affection).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and thamarah al-khilaf
Understand how the Hanafis refute these proofs: they argue that guardianship is based on need and affection, which exist in all agnates, and that the analogy to property is flawed because property transactions are repetitive. Then note the practical difference: for a mature virgin, Shafi'is require a guardian while Hanafis do not.
The hadith 'al-nikahu ila al-asabat' is the primary Hanafi dalil.

۶۴
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
کی ممارست کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے ۔ پس ہم نے ثابت پر حکم دائر کر دیا آسانی کے لئے ۔ اور ہماری دلیل وہ ہے جو ہم نے ذکر کی یعنی حاجت کا متحقق ہونا اور شفقت کا کامل ہونا اور کوئی ممارست ایسی نہیں جو بغیر شہوت کے رائے پیدا کر دے پس حکم دائر کیا جائے گا صغر پر پھر وہ جو ہمارے کلام کی تائید کرتا ہے ماقبل میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول ہے النكاح الى العصبات یعنی نکاح عصبات کے سپرد ہے بغیر فصل کے اور ترتیب عصبات میں ولایت نکاح میں ایسی ہے جیسی کہ وراثت میں اور ولی ابعد محجوب ہو گا ولی اقرب کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح . اس عبارت میں دو مسئلے زیر بحث ہیں۔ اول یہ کہ ولایت کا حق کس کو ہو گا دوم یہ کہ کس پر ہوگا پہلے مسئلے میں ائمہ کا اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ امام مالک کے نزدیک حق ولایت صرف باپ کو حاصل ہوگا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک باپ اور دادا کو حاصل ہوگا اور ہمارے نزدیک ہر ولی کو حق ولایت حاصل ہے باپ دادا ہوں یا ان کے علاوہ۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ کہ ولایت کا حق کس پر ہوگا۔ سو اس بارے میں احناف کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ ولایت کا حق صغیرہ پر ہو گا صغیرہ باکرہ ہو یا ثیبہ اور شوافع کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ ولایت باکرہ پر ہوگی صغیرہ ہو یا بالغہ۔ حاصل یہ کہ احناف کے نزدیک سبب ولایت صغر ہے اور شوافع کے نزدیک بکر ہے۔ اب چار صورتیں پیدا ہونگی ۔ دو متفق علیہ اور دو مختلف فیہ متفق علیہ میں ایک صورت ہے باکرہ صغیرہ دوم ثیبہ بالغہ، پہلی صورت میں احناف و شوافع دونوں کے نزدیک ولایت کا حق حاصل ہوگا اور دوسری صورت میں دونوں کے نزدیک ولایت حاصل نہیں ہوگی مختلف فیہ کی ایک صورت ہے باکرہ بالغہ دوسری صورت ثیبہ صغیرہ پہلی صورت یعنی باکرہ بالغہ پر شوافع کے نزدیک تو ولایت حاصل ہوگی۔ احناف کے نزدیک نہیں اور دوسری صورت یعنی ثیبہ صغیرہ پر احناف کے نزدیک تو ولایت حاصل ہوگی شوافع کے نزدیک نہیں ۔
پہلے مسئلہ میں امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ آزاد پر ولایت حاجت کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے اور صغیر اور صغیرہ میں شہوت کے معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے کوئی حاجت نہیں ہے لہذا ان پر ولایت بھی حاصل نہیں ہوگی۔ لیکن سوال یہ ہے کہ امام مالک باپ کو ولایت کا حق کیوں دیتے ہیں جواب باپ کے لئے حق ولایت خلاف قیاس نص سے ثابت ہے کیونکہ حضرت ابوبکر صدیق نے اپنی چھ سالہ صاحبزادی کا نکاح حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے کیا اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کو صحیح قرار دیا اس وجہ سے باپ کو ولایت کا حق دیدیا گیا اور چونکہ دادا باپ کے معنی میں نہیں کیونکہ دادا میں باپ کے مقابلہ میں شفقت کم ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے باپ کے ساتھ دادا کو لاحق نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ ہماری طرف سے اس کا جواب یہ ہوگا کہ ثبوت ولایت خلاف قیاس نہیں بلکہ قیاس کے عین مطابق ہے۔ اس لئے کہ نکاح متضمن ہوتا ہے کچھ مصالح کو مثلا تناسل ، ازدواج، قضاء شہوت وغیرہ۔ اور یہ مصالح ان دو آدمیوں کے درمیان حاصل ہو سکتے ہیں جن میں سے ہر ایک دوسرے کا کفو ہو۔ اور کفو کا ہر زمانہ میں ملنا ضروری نہیں اس وجہ سے ہم نے بچپن کے زمانہ میں ولایت کو ثابت کر دیا تا کہ کفو کو محفوظ رکھا جا سکے کیونکہ اگر بالغ ہونے کا انتظار کریں گے تو یہ فوت بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ولایت کا دار و مدار شفقت پر ہے اور باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ کی طرف ولایت کا حق سپرد کرنے سے شفقت کامل نہیں ہوتی۔ اس لئے کہ باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ میں نقصان شفقت بھی ہے اور بعد قرابت بھی۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ کو صغیر کے مال میں تصرف کا اختیار نہیں۔ باوجود یکہ مال مرتبہ میں کمتر ہے تو پھر نفس جو مرتبہ میں ارفع اور اعلیٰ ہے اس میں تصرف کا اختیار باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ کو بدرجہ اولیٰ نہیں ہونا چاہئے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرابت سبب ہے شفقت کا جیسا کہ باپ اور دادا میں رہی یہ بات کہ باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ میں شفقت کم ہے تو اس کا فرق اس طرح کریں گے کہ باپ اور دادا جن میں کامل شفقت ہے ان کو ولایت اجبار اور ولایت الزام دونوں کا حق دیا گیا اور باپ دادا کے علاوہ جن میں شفقت کم ہے ان کے لئے ولایت اجبار تو ثابت ہے ولایت الزام ثابت نہیں ہے۔ پس جب قرابت سبب ہے شفقت کا اور ولایت کا دار و مدار شفقت پر ہے تو جہاں شفقت پائی جائے گی وہیں وہیں ولایت کو ثابت کر دیں گے باپ دادا ہوں یا ان کے علاوہ دوسرے قرابتدار ہوں۔ ولایت اجبار اور ولایت الزام میں فرق یہ ہے کہ جن کو ولایت اجبار حاصل ہے ولایت الزام نہیں۔ ان کا کیا ہوا نکاح لازم نہیں ہوگا بلکہ بالغ ہونے کے بعد صغیرین کو خیار بلوغ حاصل ہوگا اور جس کو ولایت اجبار کے ساتھ ولایت الزام بھی حاصل ہے اس کا کیا ہوا نکاح لازم ہوگا بالغ ہونے کے بعد خیار بلوغ حاصل نہیں ہوگا ۔ امام شافعی کا قیاس کہ باپ دادا کے علاوہ کو صغیر کے مال میں تصرف کا اختیار نہیں ۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مال میں تصرف مکرر ہوتا ہے چنانچہ ولی نے ایک کو بیچا اس نے دوسرے کو دوسرے نے تیسرے کو صغیر کے بالغ ہونے تک نہ جانے کہاں سے کہاں چلا جائے پس اگر باپ دادا کے علاوہ نے صغیر کے مال میں تصرف کیا تو فعل کا تدارک ممکن نہیں ہوگا ۔ اس وجہ سے تصرف فی المال میں ولایت الزام ہی مفید ہو سکتی ہے۔ اور باپ دادا کے علاوہ کو ولایت الزام حاصل نہیں لہذا باپ دادا کے علاوہ کو مال میں تصرف کا حق بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ دوسرا مسئلہ کہ ولایت کا حق کس پر ہوگا۔ اس میں امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ثیبہ ہونا رائے کے پیدا ہونے کا سبب ہے اس لئے کہ ممارست پائی گئی ۔ پس جب ثیبہ رائے ہو گئی اور اپنے نفع نقصان کو سمجھ سکتی ہے تو اس پر ولایت کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں وہ خود مختار ہے۔ لہذا ثیبہ ہونے پر ہی آسانی کے لئے حکم دائر کر دیا گیا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ صغیر اور صغیرہ میں حاجت بھی متحقق ہے اور باپ دادا میں شفقت بھی کامل ہے اور رہی یہ بات کہ ممارست رائے پیدا کر دیتی ہے۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ بغیر شہوت کے ممارست رائے بھی پیدا نہیں کرتی بغیر شہوت کے جماع کرنا اور دیوار میں ٹکر مارنا برابر ہے۔ پس حکم صغر پر دائر کیا جائے گا ۔ چنانچہ جب صغر پایا جائے گا تو ولایت ثابت ہوگی ۔ پھر ولی کے سلسلہ میں ماقبل کے کلام کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے النکاح الى العصبات ۔ اس حدیث میں باپ دادا اور اس کے علاوہ میں کوئی فرق نہیں۔ اور ولایت نکاح کے سلسلہ میں عصبات میں ترتیب وہی ہوگی جو ترتیب وراثت میں ہے چنانچہ اقرب الاولیاء بیٹا ہے پھر پوتا اسی طرح نیچے کی طرف پھر باپ پھر دادا پھر اس کے اوپر سلسلہ وار اور ولی ابعد محروم رہے گا۔ ولی اقرب کی موجودگی میں ولی اقرب کے رہتے ہوئے ولی ابعد کو حق ولایت نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Translation will be provided in commentary. This is a detailed Urdu commentary on the Hidayah.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a detailed inter-madhhab dispute from the commentary on the Hidayah. It addresses two issues: (1) Who has the right of guardianship (wilayah) in marriage? (2) Over whom does this guardianship apply? The Hanafi position is that guardianship belongs to every agnate (asabah), not just the father (as Malikis hold) or father and grandfather (as Shafi'is hold). The Hanafi school considers minority (sighar) as the basis for guardianship, while the Shafi'i school considers virginity (bikr). Imam Malik's proof is that guardianship is needed only for those lacking judgment, and minors lack this due to absence of desire. He allows the father's guardianship by textual proof (hadith of Abu Bakr marrying his minor daughter to the Prophet). Hanafis respond that guardianship is based on need (hajah) and affection (shafaqah), which exist in all agnates, so they all have guardianship but with varying degrees of binding force (wilayat ijbar vs. wilayat ilzam). For the second issue, Shafi'is argue that a thayyib (non-virgin) has judgment (ra'y) due to marital experience, so no guardianship is needed. Hanafis respond that without desire (shahwah), marital experience does not necessarily produce sound judgment. Hence, the basis remains minority. The hadith 'al-nikahu ila al-asabat' supports that guardianship goes to all agnates, with priority given to the closest relative, similar to inheritance. The passage also distinguishes between 'wilayat ijbar' (authority to compel the marriage) and 'wilayat ilzam' (authority to make the marriage binding). Only the father and grandfather have both; other agnates have only ijbar, so the minor has the option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh) after majority.

Key Terms
ولایت (wilayah): Guardianship or authority in marriage matters, covering both the right to contract (ijbar) and the binding nature (ilzam).
عصبات (asabat): Agnate relatives on the male side, prioritized by closeness as in inheritance.
شفقت (shafaqat): Affection or compassion that motivates a guardian.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following agnates has both the authority to compel (ijbar) and binding authority (ilzam) in marriage?
A) Paternal uncle
B) Father
C) Brother
D) Cousin

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants guardianship to all agnates but restricts binding authority to the father and grandfather, balancing the minor's need for protection with their future autonomy.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Over Whom Does Guardianship Apply? Minority vs. Virginity
Explains the second issue: over whom guardianship applies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four scenarios combining minority and virginity, and state the Hanafi and Shafi'i rulings for each.

Core Idea
Hanafis base guardianship on minority; Shafi'is base it on virginity — creating four distinct scenarios.

This lesson focuses on the second issue of the guardianship dispute: over whom does the guardian have authority? The Hanafi school ties guardianship to the need of a minor, while the Shafi'i school ties it to the status of virginity. This leads to four possible scenarios with two agreements and two disagreements.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi basis for guardianship
Identify that the Hanafi school considers minority (sighar) as the sole basis (sabab) for guardianship in marriage.
The reason is that a minor lacks judgment (ra'y) and needs a guardian.
2
State the Shafi'i basis for guardianship
Identify that the Shafi'i school considers virginity (bikr) as the basis, because a virgin is assumed to lack experience and judgment.
A non-virgin (thayyib) is assumed to have gained judgment through marital experience.
3
List the four scenarios and the rulings
Enumerate the four combinations: (1) minor virgin, (2) adult non-virgin, (3) adult virgin, (4) minor non-virgin. Determine which are agreed upon and which are disputed.
Scenarios 1 and 2 are agreed: both schools require guardianship for minor virgins and neither requires for adult non-virgins. Scenarios 3 and 4 are disputed.
4
Explain the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand the practical consequences: an adult virgin (bikr balighah) needs a guardian according to Shafi'is but not Hanafis; a minor non-virgin (thayyib saghirah) needs a guardian according to Hanafis but not Shafi'is.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
کی ممارست کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے ۔ پس ہم نے ثابت پر حکم دائر کر دیا آسانی کے لئے ۔ اور ہماری دلیل وہ ہے جو ہم نے ذکر کی یعنی حاجت کا متحقق ہونا اور شفقت کا کامل ہونا اور کوئی ممارست ایسی نہیں جو بغیر شہوت کے رائے پیدا کر دے پس حکم دائر کیا جائے گا صغر پر پھر وہ جو ہمارے کلام کی تائید کرتا ہے ماقبل میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول ہے النكاح الى العصبات یعنی نکاح عصبات کے سپرد ہے بغیر فصل کے اور ترتیب عصبات میں ولایت نکاح میں ایسی ہے جیسی کہ وراثت میں اور ولی ابعد محجوب ہو گا ولی اقرب کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح . اس عبارت میں دو مسئلے زیر بحث ہیں۔ اول یہ کہ ولایت کا حق کس کو ہو گا دوم یہ کہ کس پر ہوگا پہلے مسئلے میں ائمہ کا اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ امام مالک کے نزدیک حق ولایت صرف باپ کو حاصل ہوگا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک باپ اور دادا کو حاصل ہوگا اور ہمارے نزدیک ہر ولی کو حق ولایت حاصل ہے باپ دادا ہوں یا ان کے علاوہ۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ کہ ولایت کا حق کس پر ہوگا۔ سو اس بارے میں احناف کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ ولایت کا حق صغیرہ پر ہو گا صغیرہ باکرہ ہو یا ثیبہ اور شوافع کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ ولایت باکرہ پر ہوگی صغیرہ ہو یا بالغہ۔ حاصل یہ کہ احناف کے نزدیک سبب ولایت صغر ہے اور شوافع کے نزدیک بکر ہے۔ اب چار صورتیں پیدا ہونگی ۔ دو متفق علیہ اور دو مختلف فیہ متفق علیہ میں ایک صورت ہے باکرہ صغیرہ دوم ثیبہ بالغہ، پہلی صورت میں احناف و شوافع دونوں کے نزدیک ولایت کا حق حاصل ہوگا اور دوسری صورت میں دونوں کے نزدیک ولایت حاصل نہیں ہوگی مختلف فیہ کی ایک صورت ہے باکرہ بالغہ دوسری صورت ثیبہ صغیرہ پہلی صورت یعنی باکرہ بالغہ پر شوافع کے نزدیک تو ولایت حاصل ہوگی۔ احناف کے نزدیک نہیں اور دوسری صورت یعنی ثیبہ صغیرہ پر احناف کے نزدیک تو ولایت حاصل ہوگی شوافع کے نزدیک نہیں ۔
پہلے مسئلہ میں امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ آزاد پر ولایت حاجت کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے اور صغیر اور صغیرہ میں شہوت کے معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے کوئی حاجت نہیں ہے لہذا ان پر ولایت بھی حاصل نہیں ہوگی۔ لیکن سوال یہ ہے کہ امام مالک باپ کو ولایت کا حق کیوں دیتے ہیں جواب باپ کے لئے حق ولایت خلاف قیاس نص سے ثابت ہے کیونکہ حضرت ابوبکر صدیق نے اپنی چھ سالہ صاحبزادی کا نکاح حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے کیا اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کو صحیح قرار دیا اس وجہ سے باپ کو ولایت کا حق دیدیا گیا اور چونکہ دادا باپ کے معنی میں نہیں کیونکہ دادا میں باپ کے مقابلہ میں شفقت کم ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے باپ کے ساتھ دادا کو لاحق نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ ہماری طرف سے اس کا جواب یہ ہوگا کہ ثبوت ولایت خلاف قیاس نہیں بلکہ قیاس کے عین مطابق ہے۔ اس لئے کہ نکاح متضمن ہوتا ہے کچھ مصالح کو مثلا تناسل ، ازدواج، قضاء شہوت وغیرہ۔ اور یہ مصالح ان دو آدمیوں کے درمیان حاصل ہو سکتے ہیں جن میں سے ہر ایک دوسرے کا کفو ہو۔ اور کفو کا ہر زمانہ میں ملنا ضروری نہیں اس وجہ سے ہم نے بچپن کے زمانہ میں ولایت کو ثابت کر دیا تا کہ کفو کو محفوظ رکھا جا سکے کیونکہ اگر بالغ ہونے کا انتظار کریں گے تو یہ فوت بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ولایت کا دار و مدار شفقت پر ہے اور باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ کی طرف ولایت کا حق سپرد کرنے سے شفقت کامل نہیں ہوتی۔ اس لئے کہ باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ میں نقصان شفقت بھی ہے اور بعد قرابت بھی۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ کو صغیر کے مال میں تصرف کا اختیار نہیں۔ باوجود یکہ مال مرتبہ میں کمتر ہے تو پھر نفس جو مرتبہ میں ارفع اور اعلیٰ ہے اس میں تصرف کا اختیار باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ کو بدرجہ اولیٰ نہیں ہونا چاہئے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرابت سبب ہے شفقت کا جیسا کہ باپ اور دادا میں رہی یہ بات کہ باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ میں شفقت کم ہے تو اس کا فرق اس طرح کریں گے کہ باپ اور دادا جن میں کامل شفقت ہے ان کو ولایت اجبار اور ولایت الزام دونوں کا حق دیا گیا اور باپ دادا کے علاوہ جن میں شفقت کم ہے ان کے لئے ولایت اجبار تو ثابت ہے ولایت الزام ثابت نہیں ہے۔ پس جب قرابت سبب ہے شفقت کا اور ولایت کا دار و مدار شفقت پر ہے تو جہاں شفقت پائی جائے گی وہیں وہیں ولایت کو ثابت کر دیں گے باپ دادا ہوں یا ان کے علاوہ دوسرے قرابتدار ہوں۔ ولایت اجبار اور ولایت الزام میں فرق یہ ہے کہ جن کو ولایت اجبار حاصل ہے ولایت الزام نہیں۔ ان کا کیا ہوا نکاح لازم نہیں ہوگا بلکہ بالغ ہونے کے بعد صغیرین کو خیار بلوغ حاصل ہوگا اور جس کو ولایت اجبار کے ساتھ ولایت الزام بھی حاصل ہے اس کا کیا ہوا نکاح لازم ہوگا بالغ ہونے کے بعد خیار بلوغ حاصل نہیں ہوگا ۔ امام شافعی کا قیاس کہ باپ دادا کے علاوہ کو صغیر کے مال میں تصرف کا اختیار نہیں ۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مال میں تصرف مکرر ہوتا ہے چنانچہ ولی نے ایک کو بیچا اس نے دوسرے کو دوسرے نے تیسرے کو صغیر کے بالغ ہونے تک نہ جانے کہاں سے کہاں چلا جائے پس اگر باپ دادا کے علاوہ نے صغیر کے مال میں تصرف کیا تو فعل کا تدارک ممکن نہیں ہوگا ۔ اس وجہ سے تصرف فی المال میں ولایت الزام ہی مفید ہو سکتی ہے۔ اور باپ دادا کے علاوہ کو ولایت الزام حاصل نہیں لہذا باپ دادا کے علاوہ کو مال میں تصرف کا حق بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ دوسرا مسئلہ کہ ولایت کا حق کس پر ہوگا۔ اس میں امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ثیبہ ہونا رائے کے پیدا ہونے کا سبب ہے اس لئے کہ ممارست پائی گئی ۔ پس جب ثیبہ رائے ہو گئی اور اپنے نفع نقصان کو سمجھ سکتی ہے تو اس پر ولایت کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں وہ خود مختار ہے۔ لہذا ثیبہ ہونے پر ہی آسانی کے لئے حکم دائر کر دیا گیا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ صغیر اور صغیرہ میں حاجت بھی متحقق ہے اور باپ دادا میں شفقت بھی کامل ہے اور رہی یہ بات کہ ممارست رائے پیدا کر دیتی ہے۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ بغیر شہوت کے ممارست رائے بھی پیدا نہیں کرتی بغیر شہوت کے جماع کرنا اور دیوار میں ٹکر مارنا برابر ہے۔ پس حکم صغر پر دائر کیا جائے گا ۔ چنانچہ جب صغر پایا جائے گا تو ولایت ثابت ہوگی ۔ پھر ولی کے سلسلہ میں ماقبل کے کلام کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے النکاح الى العصبات ۔ اس حدیث میں باپ دادا اور اس کے علاوہ میں کوئی فرق نہیں۔ اور ولایت نکاح کے سلسلہ میں عصبات میں ترتیب وہی ہوگی جو ترتیب وراثت میں ہے چنانچہ اقرب الاولیاء بیٹا ہے پھر پوتا اسی طرح نیچے کی طرف پھر باپ پھر دادا پھر اس کے اوپر سلسلہ وار اور ولی ابعد محروم رہے گا۔ ولی اقرب کی موجودگی میں ولی اقرب کے رہتے ہوئے ولی ابعد کو حق ولایت نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Translation will be provided in commentary. This is a detailed Urdu commentary on the Hidayah.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a detailed inter-madhhab dispute from the commentary on the Hidayah. It addresses two issues: (1) Who has the right of guardianship (wilayah) in marriage? (2) Over whom does this guardianship apply? The Hanafi position is that guardianship belongs to every agnate (asabah), not just the father (as Malikis hold) or father and grandfather (as Shafi'is hold). The Hanafi school considers minority (sighar) as the basis for guardianship, while the Shafi'i school considers virginity (bikr). Imam Malik's proof is that guardianship is needed only for those lacking judgment, and minors lack this due to absence of desire. He allows the father's guardianship by textual proof (hadith of Abu Bakr marrying his minor daughter to the Prophet). Hanafis respond that guardianship is based on need (hajah) and affection (shafaqah), which exist in all agnates, so they all have guardianship but with varying degrees of binding force (wilayat ijbar vs. wilayat ilzam). For the second issue, Shafi'is argue that a thayyib (non-virgin) has judgment (ra'y) due to marital experience, so no guardianship is needed. Hanafis respond that without desire (shahwah), marital experience does not necessarily produce sound judgment. Hence, the basis remains minority. The hadith 'al-nikahu ila al-asabat' supports that guardianship goes to all agnates, with priority given to the closest relative, similar to inheritance. The passage also distinguishes between 'wilayat ijbar' (authority to compel the marriage) and 'wilayat ilzam' (authority to make the marriage binding). Only the father and grandfather have both; other agnates have only ijbar, so the minor has the option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh) after majority.

Key Terms
صغر (sighar): Minority, the legal status of a child who has not reached puberty.
بکر (bikr): Virginity, the status of a female who has not been married.
ثیب (thayyib): A non-virgin, a female who has been previously married.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following persons requires a guardian for marriage?
A) A 20-year-old virgin woman
B) A 12-year-old non-virgin girl
C) A 25-year-old non-virgin woman
D) A 30-year-old virgin woman

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's criterion for guardianship is minority, not virginity, leading to distinct rulings from the Shafi'i school on adult virgins and minor non-virgins.

Nikah — Marriage

Father and Grandfather's Marriage Contract for Minors is Binding
Ruling with proof via ta'lil and qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that marriage by the father or grandfather is binding on minors without khiyar al-bulugh, and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) based on their complete judgment and affection.

Core Idea
Marriage by father or grandfather is binding because their judgment and affection are complete.

In Hanafi fiqh, guardianship (wilayah) in marriage is classified by authority. While nearly all guardians can contract a marriage for a minor, the minor often retains the option (khiyar al-bulugh) to annul upon puberty. However, the father and grandfather hold a special position: their marriage contracts are binding (lazim) with no option. This lesson unpacks that rule and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon and what its legal effect is. Here, the act is the marriage contract for minors performed by the father or grandfather. The ruling is that the contract is binding (lazim) and the minors have no khiyar al-bulugh.
Binding means irrevocable at the minor's choice.
2
Identify the guardians covered
Note that only the father and grandfather (when the father is deceased or absent) are mentioned. The text explicitly excludes other guardians like uncles or brothers.
The grandfather's authority is conditional on the father's absence.
3
Locate the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The text gives the reason: because they (father/grandfather) are 'complete in judgment' (kamil al-ra'y) and 'abundant in affection' (wafir al-shafaqah). This ensures they act in the minor's best interest.
This reasoning is the basis for the binding effect.
4
Analyze the analogy (qiyas)
The text compares their action to the minor giving consent after puberty. Because their judgment and affection mirror the minor's own mature consent, the contract is as binding as if the minors had directly consented.
This analogy strengthens the ruling.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Shafi'is hold that only the father has this binding authority; the grandfather does not. In their view, the grandfather ranks with other agnates, giving the minor khiyar al-bulugh.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; both schools have well-developed proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان زوجهما الاب او الجد يعنى الصغير والصغيرة فلا خيار لهما بعد بلوغهما لانهما كاملا الرأى وافرا شفقة فيلزم العقد بمباشرتهما كما اذا باشراه برضائهما بعد البلوغ ترجمہ پس اگر نکاح کیا ان دونوں کا باپ یا دادا نے یعنی صغیر اور صغیرہ کا تو ان کے لئے خیار نہیں ان دونوں کے بالغ ہونے کے بعد اس لئے کہ وہ دونوں کامل رائے اور بھر پور شفقت رکھنے والے ہیں پس عقد لازم ہوگا ان دونوں کے ارتکاب سے جیسا کہ جب دونوں نے ارتکاب کیا ان دونوں کی رضامندی سے بالغ ہونے کے بعد ۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں ولایت الزام پر تفریح بیان کی گئی ہے۔ چنانچہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر صغیر اور صغیرہ کا نکاح باپ نے کیا یا باپ کی عدم موجودگی میں دادا نے کیا تو یہ نکاح لازم ہوگا۔ اور بالغ ہونے کے بعد صغیر اور صغیرہ کو خیار بلوغ حاصل نہیں ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ کہ باپ
If the father or grandfather marries them, meaning the minor boy and girl, then they have no option (khiyar) after reaching puberty, because they (father/grandfather) are complete in judgment and abundant in affection, so the contract becomes binding by their action, just as if they acted with their consent after puberty. Translation: So if the father or grandfather marries them, meaning the minor boy and girl, then they have no khiyar after puberty, because they (father/grandfather) have complete judgment and full affection, so the contract will be binding by their action, just as if they acted with their consent after puberty. Commentary: In this passage, the exposition on binding guardianship (wilayat ilzam) is given. He says that if the father marries the minor boy and girl, or the grandfather in the absence of the father, then this marriage is binding. And after puberty, the minor boy and girl do not have the option of puberty. The proof is that... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of the Hidayah: When the father or grandfather marries a minor boy or girl, the marriage contract is binding (lazim) upon the minors, and they have no option of annulment (khiyar al-bulugh) upon reaching puberty. The reason given is that the father and grandfather possess complete judgment ('aql) and abundant affection (shafaqah). Therefore, their action is considered fully in the minor's best interest, analogous to the minors giving consent after puberty. The commentary (tashreeh) explains that this is an example of wilayat al-ilzam (binding guardianship), which is exclusive to the father and grandfather. The proof (dalil) for this ruling is only partially given in the text (cut off), but it relies on the idea that their perfect affection ensures they act in the minor's best interest, so the contract is irrevocable. This contrasts with other agnates who have only wilayat al-ijbar (authority to compel) but not ilzam, which gives the minor the option of puberty.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The legal option for a minor married under guardianship to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty, if the guardian lacked binding authority.
لازم (lazim): Binding; not subject to annulment by the minor after puberty.
شفقت (shafaqat): Affection, the quality that ensures the guardian acts in the ward's best interest.
رائے (ra'y): Judgment or discernment; the father and grandfather are said to have complete ra'y, ensuring their decisions are sound.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the rule when the grandfather (in absence of father) marries a minor girl?
A) The marriage is binding and she has no khiyar al-bulugh
B) The marriage is valid but she has khiyar al-bulugh
C) The marriage is invalid
D) The marriage requires her consent after puberty

Key Takeaway
Only the father and paternal grandfather (in the father's absence) have the authority to contract a binding marriage for minors, with no option of annulment upon puberty.

Wilayah Ijbar vs Wilayah Ilzam: The Hanafi Distinction and Shafi'i Refutation
Explaining two guardianship types and responding to Shafi'i's analogical objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between wilayah ijbar and wilayah ilzam and explain why non-father/grandfather guardians lack binding authority in marriage and property disposal, using Hanafi proofs.

Core Idea
Only father and grandfather have complete compassion; their marriage contracts are binding, others grant an option to annul.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the Hanafi view on marriage guardianship for minors. The school divides guardianship into two types: compulsory (ijbar) and binding (ilzam). Father and grandfather possess both; other agnates only possess ijbar. Imam al-Shafi'i objects using analogical reasoning, but the Hanafis respond with arguments based on compassion (shafaqah), the nature of property transactions, and a hadith. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly determining the rights of minors in marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of wilayah
The passage defines wilayah ijbar (compulsory guardianship) and wilayah ilzam (binding guardianship). Father and grandfather have both; others have only ijbar.
Wilayah ijbar allows contracting marriage without the minor's consent but not binding; wilayah ilzam makes the contract binding with no option to annul.
2
Understand the basis: compassion (shafaqah)
Wilayah depends on shafaqah. Father and grandfather have complete shafaqah; other relatives have less. Therefore, only they qualify for ilzam.
Shafaqah is the underlying cause ('illah) for the degree of guardianship.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i qiyas on property disposal
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since non-father/grandfather guardians cannot dispose of a minor's property, they should also not have binding marriage authority. The Hanafi response distinguishes between property and marriage: property transactions are recurrent and may become irreparable, requiring binding authority (ilzam).
The difference in illa (property vs. marriage) breaks the analogy.
4
Examine the second dispute: basis for wilayah
Shafi'i holds that puberty (shaybah) ends the need for guardianship because one then has sound opinion. Hanafi responds that sound opinion requires sexual desire (shahwah); without it, practice alone does not produce sound judgment. Thus, guardianship continues until minority ends with full sexual maturity.
The ruling is tied to minority (sighar), not merely puberty.
5
Apply the hadith on agnatic guardianship
The hadith 'al-nikahu ila al-'asabat' is cited to show that all agnates have a role. The order of guardianship follows the order of inheritance: nearest excludes farther.
The hadith is general; the distinction between ijbar and ilzam is derived from shafaqah.

شفقت ہے ان کو ولایت اجبار اور ولایت الزام دونوں کا حق دیا گیا اور باپ دادا کے علاوہ جن میں شفقت کم ہے ان کے لئے ولایت اجبار تو ثابت ہے ولایت الزام ثابت نہیں ہے۔ پس جب قرابت سبب ہے شفقت کا اور ولایت کا دارو مدار شفقت پر ہے تو جہاں شفقت پائی جائے گی وہیں وہیں ولایت کو ثابت کر دیں گے باپ دادا ہوں یا انکے علاوہ دوسرے قرابتدار ہوں۔ ولایت اجبار اور ولایت الزام میں فرق یہ ہے کہ جن کو ولایت اجبار حاصل ہے دوسرے نے تیسرے کو صغیر کے بالغ ہونے تک نہ جانے کہاں سے کہاں چلا جائے پس اگر باپ دادا کے علاوہ نے صغیر کے مال میں تصرف کیا تو فعل کا تدارک ممکن نہیں ہوگا ۔ اس وجہ سے تصرف فی المال میں ولایت الزام ہی مفید ہوسکتی ہے۔ اور باپ دادا کے علاوہ کو ولایت الزام حاصل نہیں لہذا باپ دادا کے علاوہ کو مال میں تصرف کا حق بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ دوسرا مسئلہ کہ ولایت کا حق کس پر ہوگا۔ آسمیں امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شیبہ ہونا رائے کے پیدا ہونے کا سبب ہے اس لئے کہ ممارست پائی گئی ۔ پس جب شیبہ ڈی رائے ہو گئی اور اپنے نفع نقصان کو سمجھ سکتی ہے تو اس پر ولایت کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں وہ خود مختار ہے۔ لہذا شیبہ ہونے پر ہی آسانی کے لئے حکم دائر کر دیا گیا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ صغیر اور صغیرہ میں حاجت بھی متحقق ہے اور باپ دادا میں شفقت بھی کامل ہے اور رہی یہ بات کہ ممارست رائے پیدا کر دیتی ہے۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ بغیر شہوت کے ممارست رائے بھی پیدا نہیں کرتی بغیر شہوت کے جماع کرنا اور دیوار میں ٹکر مار نا برابر ہے۔ پس حکم صغر پر دائر کیا جائے گا ۔ چنانچہ جب صغر پایا جائے گا تو ولایت ثابت ہوگی ۔ پھرولی کے سلسلہ میں ماقبل کے کلام کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے النکاح الى العصبات ۔ اس حدیث میں باپ دادا اور اس کے علاوہ میں کوئی فرق نہیں۔ اور ولایت نکاح کے سلسلہ میں عصبات میں ترتیب وہی ہوگی جو ترتیب وراثت میں ہے چنانچہ اقرب الاولیاء بیٹا ہے پھر پوتا اسی طرح نیچے کی طرف پھر باپ پھر دادا پھر اس کے اوپر سلسلہ وار اور ولی ابعد محروم رہے گا۔ ولی اقرب کی موجودگی میں ولی اقرب کے رہتے ہوئے ولی ابعد کو حق ولایت نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
(They have compassion, so both wilayah ijbar and wilayah ilzam are given to them. For others besides father and grandfather, in whom compassion is less, wilayah ijbar is established but wilayah ilzam is not. So when relationship is the cause of compassion, and wilayah depends on compassion, then wherever compassion is found, we will establish wilayah, whether they are father and grandfather or other relatives. The difference between wilayah ijbar and wilayah ilzam is that those who have wilayah ijbar but not wilayah ilzam, their marriage contract is not binding; rather after puberty the minors will have khiyar al-bulugh. And those who have wilayah ijbar together with wilayah ilzam, their marriage contract is binding; after puberty they will not have khiyar al-bulugh. Imam Shafi'i's analogy is that others besides father and grandfather do not have authority to dispose of the minor's property. The answer to this is that disposal of property is recurrent; the guardian sells to one, who sells to another, who sells to a third, and by the time the minor reaches puberty, it may have gone far away. So if someone other than father or grandfather disposes of the minor's property, rectification of the act may not be possible. For this reason, in disposal of property, only wilayah ilzam can be beneficial. And others besides father and grandfather do not have wilayah ilzam, so they do not have the right to dispose of property. Second issue: on whom will the right of wilayah be? Regarding this, Imam Shafi'i's evidence is that reaching puberty is a cause for the emergence of opinion, because practice (mumarasah) is obtained. So when one becomes pubescent and of opinion, and understands one's own benefit and harm, then there is no need for wilayah; he is independent. Therefore the ruling was applied upon puberty for convenience. Our evidence is that in the minor boy and girl, need is also realized, and in father and grandfather, compassion is also complete. As for the statement that practice produces opinion, we say: practice without sexual desire does not produce opinion; intercourse without desire is like hitting the wall with one's head. So the ruling will be applied upon minority. Thus when minority is found, wilayah will be established. Furthermore, the previous discussion about the guardian is also supported by this hadith: 'Marriage belongs to the 'asabat (agnates).' In this hadith there is no difference between father and grandfather and others. And in the matter of marriage guardianship, the order of 'asabat is the same as the order of inheritance. Thus the nearest guardian is the son, then grandson, and so on downwards, then father, then grandfather, then upwards in order, and the distant guardian will be excluded. In the presence of the nearer guardian, the distant guardian will not be given the right of wilayah. And Allah knows best what is correct.)
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The text begins by explaining the difference between wilayah ijbar (compulsory guardianship) and wilayah ilzam (binding guardianship). According to the Hanafi school, both types are granted to the father and grandfather due to their complete compassion (shafaqah). Other relatives, having less compassion, only have wilayah ijbar but not wilayah ilzam. This means that if a non-father/grandfather marries a minor, the minor retains the option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh) to cancel the marriage after maturity. The author then addresses the objection of Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that since non-father/grandfather guardians cannot dispose of a minor's property, they also cannot contract marriage with binding effect. The Hanafi response is that property transactions are recurrent and may be impossible to rectify once executed, so only the binding authority (ilzam) suffices—and that is absent in non-father/grandfather guardians. Regarding the basis of wilayah, Imam Shafi'i holds that puberty ends the need for guardianship because one can then form reasoned opinion. The Hanafi response argues that puberty alone is insufficient; what matters is sexual maturity (shahwah) that generates true opinion. Without it, practice (mumarasah) does not produce sound opinion. Therefore, the ruling is tied to minority (sighar), not puberty. The passage then cites the hadith 'al-nikahu ila al-'asabat' to support that all agnates have a role, and the order of guardianship follows the order of inheritance: nearer excludes farther.

Key Terms
ولایت اجبار (wilayah ijbar): Guardianship that allows the guardian to contract marriage without the minor's consent, but the contract is not binding until confirmation after puberty.
ولایت الزام (wilayah ilzam): Guardianship that makes the marriage contract binding with no option of annulment after puberty.
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option of annulment granted to a minor upon reaching puberty if the marriage was contracted by a guardian without binding authority.
شفقت (shafaqah): Compassion or tenderness that justifies the grant of guardianship; father and grandfather have the highest degree.
عصبات ('asabat): Agnatic relatives (male line) who have priority for marriage guardianship; order follows inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why can a non-father/grandfather guardian not dispose of a minor's property?
A) Because they lack sufficient compassion (shafaqah)
B) Because property disposal requires binding authority (wilayah ilzam), which they do not have, and transactions may be irreparable
C) Because they are not allowed to make any financial decisions for the minor
D) Because the minor has already reached puberty

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, only father and grandfather have binding authority (wilayah ilzam) in marriage and property; other agnates have only compulsory authority (wilayah ijbar), granting the minor the right to annul the marriage upon puberty.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
6 min
No Khiyar al-Bulugh When Father or Grandfather Marries Minors
Ruling statement with talil (causal reasoning)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that khiyar al-bulugh is not available when father or grandfather marries a minor and explain the reasoning based on complete opinion and compassion.

Core Idea
Father and grandfather's marriage of a minor is binding; no option upon puberty.

This lesson examines the first part of the text which establishes a key exception: when the marriage of a minor is contracted by the father or grandfather, the marriage is fully binding. The reasoning hinges on the completeness of their opinion and compassion. Understanding this baseline is crucial before exploring the dispute about other guardians.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State that khiyar al-bulugh is absent when father or grandfather marries a minor. The marriage is binding immediately.
This is the default rule for these guardians.
2
Locate the illa (causal reason)
The text gives the reason: father and grandfather have complete opinion (kamal al-ra'y) and abundant compassion (wafar al-shafaqah). This makes their judgment equivalent to the minor's own consent after maturity.
The completeness is unique to these two guardians.
3
Note the consequence
Because of the complete illa, the contract is binding (lazim) just as if the minor had consented after puberty. No subsequent option can annul it.
This binding effect is called wilayat al-ilzam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باپ اور دادا نے صغیر اور صغیرہ کا نکاح کرایا تو بلوغت کے بعد دونوں کو خیار نہیں
فان زوجهما الاب او الجد يعنى الصغير والصغيرة فلا خيار لهما بعد بلوغهما لانهما كاملا الرأى وافرا شفقة فيلزم العقد بمباشرتهما كما اذا باشراه بـرضـائهـمـا بعد البلوغ ترجمہ پس اگر نکاح کیا ان دونوں کا باپ یا دادا نے یعنی صغیر اور صغیرہ کا تو ان کے لئے خیار نہیں ان دونوں کے بالغ ہونے کے بعد اس لئے کہ وہ دونوں کامل رائے اور بھر پور شفقت رکھنے والے ہیں پس عقد لازم ہوگا ان دونوں کے ارتکاب سے جیسا کہ جب دونوں نے ارتکاب کیا ان دونوں کی رضامندی سے بالغ ہونے کے بعد ۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں ولایت الزام پر تفریح بیان کی گئی ہے۔ چنانچہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر صغیر اور صغیرہ کا نکاح باپ نے کیا یا باپ کی عدم موجودگی میں دادا نے کیا تو یہ نکاح لازم ہوگا۔ اور بالغ ہونے کے بعد صغیر اور صغیرہ کو خیار بلوغ حاصل نہیں ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ کہ باپ اور دادا دونوں کامل رائے اور بھر پور شفقت رکھتے ہیں اس لئے کہ دونوں کا کیا ہوا نکاح لازم ہوگا جیسے اگر بالغ ہونے کے بعد باپ یا دادا نے ان دونوں کی رضا مندی سے نکاح کیا ہے تو وہ نکاح لازم ہوگا۔
اگر باپ اور داد کے علاوہ کسی نے نکاح کرایا تو دونوں کو جیار ہے
وان زوجها غير الاب والجد فلكل واحد منهما الخيار اذا بلغ ان شاء اقام على النكاح وان شاء فسخ وهذا عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وقال ابويوسف لاخيار لهما اعتبارا بالاب والجد ولهما ان قرابة الاخ ناقصة والنقصان يشعر بقصور الشفقة فيتطرق الخلل الى المقاصد عسى والتدارک ممكن بخيار الادراك واطلاق الجواب في غير الاب والجديتناول الام والقاضى وهو الصحيح من الرواية لقصور الراى فى احدهما ونقصان الشفقة فى الآخر فيتخير ويشترط فيه القضاء بخلاف خيار العتق لان الفسخ هنالد فع ضرر محفى وهو تمكن الخلل ولهذا يشمل الذكر والانثى فجعل الزامافي حق الآخر فيفتقر الى القضاء وخيار العتق لدفع ضرر جلى و هو زيادة الملك عليها ولهذا يختص بالانثى فاعتبر دفعا و الدفع لا يفتقر الى القضاء
ترجمہ اور اگر نکاح کیا صغیر اور صغیرہ کا باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ نے تو ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے لئے خیار ہے جب بالغ ہو جائے جی چاہے نکاح کو باقی رکھے اور جی چاہے فسخ کر دے اور یہ طرفین کے نزدیک ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ ان دونوں کو خیار نہیں قیاس کرتے ہوئے باپ اور دادا پر۔ اور ان دونوں کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بھائی کی قرابت ناقص ہے اور نقصان قرابت خبر دیتا ہے قصور شفقت کی۔ پس مقاصد میں خلل کا واقع ہونا ممکن ہے اور تلافی ممکن ہے خیار بلوغ سے اور باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ میں حکم کا مطلق ہونا شامل ہے ماں اور قاضی کو ۔ اور یہ صحیح روایت ہے رائے کے ناقص ہونے کی وجہ سے ان دونوں میں سے ایک مین اور نقصان شفقت دوسرے میں لہذا اختیار ہیگا اور شرط لگائی گئی خیار بلوغ میں قضاء قاضی کی ۔ بخلاف خیار عتق کے اس لئے کہ یہاں فتح ضرر خفی کو دور کرنے کیلئے ہے اور وہ ضرر خفی خلل کا ممکن ہونا ہے۔ اور اسی وجہ سے شامل ہوگا ذکر اور مؤنث دونوں کو پس دوسرے کے حق میں الزام قرار دیا جائے گا لہذا قضاء کا محتاج ہوگا اور خیار عتق ضرر جلی کو دور کرنے کیلئے ہے اور وہ ضرر جلی معتقہ پر ملک کا زیادہ ہونا ہے اور اسی وجہ سے محفوظ ہوگا مونث کے ساتھ پس اعتبار کیا جائے گا دفع اور دفع قضا کامحتاج نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں ولایت اجبار پر تفریح بیان کی ہے۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر صغیر اور صغیرہ کا نکاح باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ نے کیا تو بالغ ہونے کے بعد صغیرین میں سے ہر ایک کو خیار بلوغ کے تحت نکاح کو باقی رکھنے اور نسخ کر دینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ یہ حکم طرفین کے نزدیک ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ صغیرین کو خیار بلوغ حاصل نہیں ہوگا ۔ امام ابو یوسف غیراب اور جد کو قیاس کرتے ہیں اب اور جد پر۔ یعنی جس طرح باپ اور دادا کا کیا ہوا نکاح لازم ہوتا ہے بالغ ہونے کے بعد اس کو فسخ نہیں کیا جا سکتا اسی طرح غیر باپ اور دادا کا کیا ہوا نکاح بھی لازم ہو گا۔ بالغ ہونے کے بعد صغیرین کو فسخ کا اختیار نہیں ہو گا۔ مقیس اور مقیس علیہ کے درمیان جامع قرابت ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک باپ دادا کی طرح غیر باپ اور غیر دادا کو بھی ولایت اجبار کے ساتھ ولایت الزام حاصل ہوگی۔
Father and grandfather married the minor boy and girl, so after puberty both have no option. (Then the Arabic matn: 'If the father or grandfather marries them [the minor boy and girl], there is no option for them after puberty, because they [the guardians] are complete in opinion and abundant in compassion, so the contract is binding by their action, just as if they acted with their consent after puberty.') Commentary: In this expression, the binding guardianship is explained. Thus it is stated: If the father or the grandfather (in the father's absence) marries the minor boy and girl, this marriage is binding. After puberty, the minors do not have khiyar al-bulugh. The evidence is that father and grandfather both have complete opinion and abundant compassion; thus their marriage contract is binding, just as if after puberty they married them with their consent. (Then heading) If someone other than father and grandfather marries them, both have the option. (Arabic matn: 'If someone other than the father and grandfather marries her, each of them has the option when they reach puberty: if they wish they may stay in the marriage, and if they wish they may annul. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: They have no option, analogizing to the father and grandfather. And these two [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad] argue that the brother's relationship is deficient, and deficiency indicates insufficiency of compassion; thus defect may enter the objectives, and rectification is possible through the option of comprehension (khiyar al-Idrak). The absolute answer regarding other than father and grandfather includes the mother and the judge, and this is the correct transmission, due to deficiency of opinion in one of them [mother] and deficiency of compassion in the other [judge]; thus they have option. And it is conditioned in this that [the annulment] requires a court decree, unlike the option of emancipation (khiyar al-'itq), because the annulment here is to remove a hidden harm (darar khafi), which is the potential for defect. For this reason it applies to both male and female, so it is made binding in the right of the other, thus it requires a court decree. And the option of emancipation is to remove a manifest harm (darar jali), which is the increase of ownership over the slave-woman, and for this reason it is specific to the female; so it is considered a repelling, and repelling does not require a court decree.' Translation: And if the marriage of the minor boy and girl is performed by someone other than father and grandfather, then each of them has an option when they reach puberty: if they wish they may keep the marriage and if they wish they may annul. This is according to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: They have no option, analogizing to father and grandfather. And the evidence of these two is that the brother's relationship is deficient, and deficiency of relationship indicates insufficiency of compassion; thus defect may occur in the objectives, and rectification is possible through the option of puberty. And the absolute answer regarding other than father and grandfather includes the mother and the judge, and this is the correct transmission, due to deficiency of opinion in one of them and deficiency of compassion in the other; therefore they have an option. And condition is laid in the option of puberty that it requires a court decree, unlike the option of emancipation, because the annulment here is to remove a hidden harm, which is the potential for defect. And for this reason it includes both male and female, so it is made binding in the right of the other, thus it requires a court decree. And the option of emancipation is to remove a manifest harm, which is the increase of ownership over the slave-woman, and for this reason it is specific to the female; so it is considered a repelling, and repelling does not require a court decree. Commentary: In this expression, the compulsory guardianship is explained. The issue is that if the marriage of the minor boy and girl is performed by someone other than father and grandfather, then after puberty each of the minors has the option under khiyar al-bulugh to keep or annul the marriage. This ruling is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Imam Abu Yusuf said that the minors have no khiyar al-bulugh. Imam Abu Yusuf analogizes other than father and grandfather to father and grandfather. That is, just as the marriage performed by father and grandfather is binding and cannot be annulled after puberty, similarly the marriage performed by other than father and grandfather will also be binding. After puberty, the minors will have no option to annul. The common link between the analogized and the analogized-upon is relationship. The conclusion is that according to Abu Yusuf, other than father and grandfather also have both wilayah ijbar and wilayah ilzam like father and grandfather.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute focusing on a specific ruling. The text presents two cases: (1) If the father or grandfather marries a minor, the marriage is binding and there is no khiyar al-bulugh after puberty. The reason given is that these guardians possess complete reasoned opinion (ra'y) and abundant compassion (shafaqah), so their action is equivalent to the minor's own consent after maturity. (2) If someone other than father or grandfather (e.g., brother, uncle, mother, judge) marries the minor, the majority position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad is that the minor retains the option to confirm or annul the marriage upon reaching puberty. This is because the relationship of such guardians is deficient: some lack full reasoned opinion (like the mother) while others lack full compassion (like the judge). Thus, to protect the minor, a window for rectification is provided. However, Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, analogizing all guardians to father and grandfather, arguing that since all guardians share the common factor of relationship, they should all have binding authority. The text then contrasts this khiyar al-bulugh with khiyar al-'itq (option of emancipation). The former requires a court decree because it removes a hidden harm (darar khafi) and applies to both sexes. The latter does not require a court decree because it removes a manifest harm (darar jali) and is specific to female slaves. The commentary clarifies that Abu Yusuf's view is that non-father/grandfather guardians also have wilayah ilzam.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option of annulment given to a minor upon reaching puberty if the marriage was contracted by a guardian without full binding authority (i.e., not father/grandfather).
ضرر خفی (darar khafi): Hidden harm; the potential for defect in the marriage contract due to insufficient compassion or opinion of the guardian.
قضاء (qada): Court decree or judicial ruling; required for annulment in khiyar al-bulugh but not in khiyar al-'itq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a minor NOT have khiyar al-bulugh upon reaching puberty?
A) When the marriage was contracted by the mother.
B) When the marriage was contracted by the father or grandfather.
C) When the marriage was contracted by the brother.
D) When the marriage was contracted by the judge.

Key Takeaway
When father or grandfather marries a minor, the marriage is binding and khiyar al-bulugh does not apply.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Khiyar al-Bulugh When Other Guardians Marry Minors: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Comparison with Khiyar al-'Itq
Intra-Hanafi dispute with comparative talil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad vs. Abu Yusuf regarding khiyar al-bulugh when a non-father/grandfather guardian marries a minor, and distinguish khiyar al-bulugh from khiyar al-'itq in terms of requiring a court decree.

Core Idea
Other guardians' marriage of a minor gives the minor an option upon puberty, requiring a court decree, unlike khiyar al-'itq.

This lesson delves into the intra-Hanafi disagreement concerning khiyar al-bulugh when the guardian is not the father or grandfather. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad grant the minor an option at puberty, while Imam Abu Yusuf binds the marriage entirely. The text also contrasts this option with khiyar al-'itq, highlighting the requirement of a court decree due to the nature of the harm.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, when a guardian other than father or grandfather marries a minor, the minor has the option (khiyar al-bulugh) upon reaching puberty: they can confirm or annul the marriage.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
State Abu Yusuf's opposing view
Abu Yusuf holds that the minor has no option, because he analogizes all guardians to father and grandfather based on the common factor of guardianship relationship.
This is valid ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that the analogy fails because the relationship of non-father/grandfather guardians is deficient, which indicates deficiency in compassion. This deficiency can lead to hidden harm in the marriage, which can only be rectified by giving the minor an option.
The text specifically mentions the brother's deficient relationship.
4
Note the condition of qada (court decree)
The text states that khiyar al-bulugh requires a court decree (qada) for annulment, unlike khiyar al-'itq. This is because khiyar al-bulugh removes a hidden harm (darar khafi), which requires judicial determination.
The hidden harm is the potential for defect in the marriage due to insufficient compassion.
5
Compare with khiyar al-'itq
Khiyar al-'itq (option of emancipation) applies to female slaves who were married without consent. It does not require a court decree because it removes a manifest harm (darar jali), i.e., the husband's ownership over the slave-woman. The harm is obvious and does not need judicial investigation.
Khiyar al-'itq is also specific to females, while khiyar al-bulugh applies to both sexes.

Father and grandfather married the minor boy and girl, so after puberty both have no option. (Then the Arabic matn: 'If the father or grandfather marries them [the minor boy and girl], there is no option for them after puberty, because they [the guardians] are complete in opinion and abundant in compassion, so the contract is binding by their action, just as if they acted with their consent after puberty.') Commentary: In this expression, the binding guardianship is explained. Thus it is stated: If the father or the grandfather (in the father's absence) marries the minor boy and girl, this marriage is binding. After puberty, the minors do not have khiyar al-bulugh. The evidence is that father and grandfather both have complete opinion and abundant compassion; thus their marriage contract is binding, just as if after puberty they married them with their consent. (Then heading) If someone other than father and grandfather marries them, both have the option. (Arabic matn: 'If someone other than the father and grandfather marries her, each of them has the option when they reach puberty: if they wish they may stay in the marriage, and if they wish they may annul. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: They have no option, analogizing to the father and grandfather. And the option of emancipation is to remove a manifest harm (darar jali), which is the increase of ownership over the slave-woman, and for this reason it is specific to the female; so it is considered a repelling, and repelling does not require a court decree.' This is according to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: They have no option, analogizing to father and grandfather. And the absolute answer regarding other than father and grandfather includes the mother and the judge, and this is the correct transmission, due to deficiency of opinion in one of them and deficiency of compassion in the other; therefore they have an option. And the option of emancipation is to remove a manifest harm, which is the increase of ownership over the slave-woman, and for this reason it is specific to the female; so it is considered a repelling, and repelling does not require a court decree. This ruling is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Imam Abu Yusuf said that the minors have no khiyar al-bulugh. Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute focusing on a specific ruling. The text presents two cases: (1) If the father or grandfather marries a minor, the marriage is binding and there is no khiyar al-bulugh after puberty. The reason given is that these guardians possess complete reasoned opinion (ra'y) and abundant compassion (shafaqah), so their action is equivalent to the minor's own consent after maturity. (2) If someone other than father or grandfather (e.g., brother, uncle, mother, judge) marries the minor, the majority position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad is that the minor retains the option to confirm or annul the marriage upon reaching puberty. This is because the relationship of such guardians is deficient: some lack full reasoned opinion (like the mother) while others lack full compassion (like the judge). Thus, to protect the minor, a window for rectification is provided. However, Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, analogizing all guardians to father and grandfather, arguing that since all guardians share the common factor of relationship, they should all have binding authority. The text then contrasts this khiyar al-bulugh with khiyar al-'itq (option of emancipation). The former requires a court decree because it removes a hidden harm (darar khafi) and applies to both sexes. The latter does not require a court decree because it removes a manifest harm (darar jali) and is specific to female slaves. The commentary clarifies that Abu Yusuf's view is that non-father/grandfather guardians also have wilayah ilzam.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option of annulment given to a minor upon reaching puberty if the marriage was contracted by a guardian without full binding authority (i.e., not father/grandfather).
خیار عتق (khiyar al-'itq): The option for a female slave to annul her marriage upon emancipation if she was married without her consent.
ضرر خفی (darar khafi): Hidden harm; the potential for defect in the marriage contract due to insufficient compassion or opinion of the guardian.
ضرر جلی (darar jali): Manifest harm; the overt disadvantage of the enslaved woman being owned by her husband.
قضاء (qada): Court decree or judicial ruling; required for annulment in khiyar al-bulugh but not in khiyar al-'itq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the text, why does khiyar al-bulugh require a court decree while khiyar al-'itq does not?
A) Because khiyar al-bulugh applies to both sexes, while khiyar al-'itq applies only to females.
B) Because when you annul a marriage by khiyar al-bulugh, you remove a hidden harm that needs judicial determination, while khiyar al-'itq removes a manifest harm.
C) Because the minor is not mature enough to make the decision alone.
D) Because the guardian must be present in court.

Key Takeaway
Non-father/grandfather guardians' marriage gives the minor an option at puberty, which requires a court decree, in contrast to khiyar al-'itq.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Khiyar al-Bulugh: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Its Basis
Explains khiyar al-bulugh for minors married by non-father/grandfather guardians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on khiyar al-bulugh for minors married by non-father/grandfather guardians, explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and evaluate the evidence from deficient compassion.

Core Idea
A minor married by a non-father guardian has the option to annul at puberty because deficient compassion creates potential harm.

When a minor is married by a guardian who is not their father or grandfather, a key question arises: is the marriage binding or does the minor retain an option upon reaching puberty? This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (who grant the option) and Abu Yusuf (who denies it). We will explore the legal reasoning based on the concept of deficient compassion and see how this applies to guardians like the mother and judge.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the act: a minor married by a guardian other than the father or grandfather. State Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's position (option exists) and Abu Yusuf's position (no option, marriage binding).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Understand Abu Yusuf's qiyas
Abu Yusuf draws an analogy with the father and grandfather, arguing that since both are guardians, the marriage should be binding.
This is qiyas jali based on the common attribute of guardianship.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The majority respond that the analogy is flawed because the relationship of other guardians (e.g., brother) is deficient, indicating deficient compassion. Thus there is a possibility of harm, and the option at puberty allows rectification.
This is qiyas khafi: deficiency in relationship implies deficiency in compassion.
4
Apply the logic to mother and judge
The mother has perfect compassion but imperfect judgment; the judge has perfect judgment but imperfect compassion. Both lack one perfection, so they have wilayat al-ijbar (authority to contract) but not wilayat al-ilzam (binding authority). Hence their marriages are also subject to khiyar al-bulugh.
This is the correct transmission (sahih al-riwayah).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is the relied-upon view for fatwa, as supported by al-Hidayah.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah.
