كتاب النكاح

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم

اور دادا دونوں کامل رائے اور بھر پور شفقت رکھتے ہیں اس لئے کہ دونوں کا کیا ہوا نکاح لازم ہوگا جیسے اگر بالغ ہونے کے بعد باپ یا دادا نے ان دونوں کی رضا مندی سے نکاح کیا ہے تو وہ نکاح لازم ہوگا۔
اگر باپ اور داد کے علاوہ کسی نے نکاح کرایا تو دونوں کو جیار ہے
و ان زوجها غير الاب والجد فلكل واحد منهما الخيار اذا بلغ ان شاء اقام على النكاح وان شاء فسخ وهذا عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وقال ابويوسف لاخيار لهما اعتبارا بالاب والجد ولهما ان قرابة الاخ ناقصة والنقصان يشعر بقصور الشفقة فيتطرق الخلل الى المقاصد عسى والتدارک ممکن بخيار الادراك واطلاق الجواب في غير الاب والجديتناول الام والقاضى وهو الصحيح من الرواية لقصور الراى فى احدهما ونقصان الشفقة فى الآخر فيتخير ويشترط فيه القضاء بخلاف خيار العتق لان الفسخ هنالد فع ضرر محفى وهو تمكن الخلل ولهذا يشمل الذكر والانثى فجعل الزامافي حق الآخر فيفتقر الى القضاء وخيار العتق لدفع ضرر جلى و هو زيادة الملك عليها ولهذا يختص بالانثى فاعتبر دفعا و الدفع لا يفتقر الى القضاء

ترجمہ اور اگر نکاح کیا صغیر اور صغیرہ کا باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ نے تو ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے لئے خیار ہے جب بالغ ہو جائے جی چاہے نکاح کو باقی رکھے اور جی چاہے فسخ کر دے اور یہ طرفین کے نزدیک ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ ان دونوں کو خیار نہیں قیاس کرتے ہوئے باپ اور دادا پر۔ اور ان دونوں کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بھائی کی قرابت ناقص ہے اور نقصان قرابت خبر دیتا ہے قصور شفقت کی۔ پس مقاصد میں خلل کا واقع ہونا ممکن ہے اور تلافی ممکن ہے خیار بلوغ سے اور باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ میں حکم کا مطلق ہونا شامل ہے ماں اور قاضی کو ۔ اور یہ صحیح روایت ہے رائے کے ناقص ہونے کی وجہ سے ان دونوں میں سے ایک مین اور نقصان شفقت دوسرے میں لہذا اختیار ہیگا اور شرط لگائی گئی خیار بلوغ میں قضاء قاضی کی ۔ بخلاف خیار عتق کے اس لئے کہ یہاں فتح ضرر خفی کو دور کرنے کیلئے ہے اور وہ ضرر خفی خلل کا ممکن ہونا ہے۔ اور اسی وجہ سے شامل ہوگا ذکر اور مؤنث دونوں کو پس دوسرے کے حق میں الزام قرار دیا جائے گا لہذا قضاء کا محتاج ہوگا اور خیار عتق ضرر جلی کو دور کرنے کیلئے ہے اور وہ ضرر جلی معتقہ پر ملک کا زیادہ ہونا ہے اور اسی وجہ سے محفوظ ہوگا مونث کے ساتھ پس اعتبار کیا جائے گا دفع اور دفع قضا کامحتاج نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں ولایت اجبار پر تفریح بیان کی ہے۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر صغیر اور صغیرہ کا نکاح باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ نے کیا تو بالغ ہونے کے بعد صغیرین میں سے ہر ایک کو خیار بلوغ کے تحت نکاح کو باقی رکھنے اور نسخ کر دینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ یہ حکم طرفین کے نزدیک ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ صغیرین کو خیار بلوغ حاصل نہیں ہوگا ۔ امام ابو یوسف غیراب اور جد کو قیاس کرتے ہیں اب اور جد پر۔ یعنی جس طرح باپ اور دادا کا کیا ہوا نکاح لازم ہوتا ہے بالغ ہونے کے بعد اس کو فسخ نہیں کیا جا سکتا اسی طرح غیر باپ اور دادا کا کیا ہوا نکاح بھی لازم ہو گا۔ بالغ ہونے کے بعد صغیرین کو فسخ کا اختیار نہیں ہو گا۔ مقیس اور مقیس علیہ کے درمیان جامع قرابت ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک باپ دادا کی طرح غیر باپ اور غیر دادا کو بھی ولایت اجبار کے ساتھ ولایت الزام حاصل ہوگی۔

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم

كتاب النكاح

طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ مثلاً بھائی کی قرابت باپ دادا کی قرابت سے ناقص ہے۔ اور نقصان قرابت دلیل ہے نقصان شفقت کی. پس نقصان شفقت کی وجہ سے باپ دادا کے علاوہ کے کئے ہوئے نکاح میں خلل کا واقع ہو نا ممکن ہے۔ اور نقصان شفقت کی وجہ سے مقاصد نکاح میں جو خلل کا امکان پیدا ہو گیا ہے خیار بلوغ کے ذریعہ اس کی تلافی بھی ممکن ہے۔ پس اس خلل کی تلافی کے لئے صغیرین کو خیار بلوغ حاصل ہوگا۔ اور باپ دادا کے علاوہ کا کیا ہوا نکاح لازم نہیں ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ طرفین کے نزدیک غیراب اور غیر جد کو ولایت اجبار تو حاصل ہے لیکن ولایت الزام حاصل نہیں ۔
واطلاق الجواب کا منشاء یہ ہے کہ حکم کا اطلاق باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ میں ماں اور قاضی کو بھی شامل ہے مطلب یہ ہے کہ ماں اور قاضی کو بھی ولایت اجبار حاصل ہے ولایت الزام حاصل نہیں لہذا ان کا کیا ہوا نکاح بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا بلکہ بالغ ہونے کے بعد صغیرین کو خیار بلوغ کے تحت فسخ کر دینے کا حق ہے صحیح روایت یہی ہے اگر چہ ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ قاضی نے اگر کسی یتیمہ کا نکاح کر دیا تو اس کو خیار بلوغ حاصل نہیں ہوگا بلکہ نکاح لازم ہوگا اور وجہ یہ ہے کہ قاضی کے لئے مال اور نفس دونوں میں ولایت نامہ ثابت ہے لہذا قاضی کی ولایت قوۃ میں باپ اور دادا کی ولایت کے برابر ہوگی۔
روایت صحیحہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ولایت الزام کے لئے دو چیزیں ضروری ہیں کمال رائے اور کمال شفقت اگر یہ دونوں چیزیں پائی یہ ہیں اور گئیں تو ولایت الزام حاصل ہوگی ۔ اور اگر دونوں میں سے ایک چیز پائی گئی تو صرف ولایت اجبار حاصل ہوگی۔ ولایت الزام نہیں۔ یہاں یہی بات ہے کیونکہ ماں میں کمال شفقت ہے کمال رائے نہیں ، اور قاضی میں کمال رائے ہے کمال شفقت نہیں ۔ پس ان دونوں کو ولایت اجبار تو حاصل ہوگی ولایت الزام نہیں۔ لہذا ان دونوں کا کیا ہوا نکاح لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ اور صغیر میں کو فسخ کر دینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ خیار بلوغ کی وجہ سے اگر نکاح فسخ کیا گیا تو اسمیں قضاء قاضی شرط ہے یعینی صغیرین سے کسی ایک کا فسخ کہنا کافی نہیں ہوگا ، بلکہ قاضی کی عدالت میں مقدمہ پیش کریں۔ پھر قاضی فسخ نکاح کا حکم دے برخلاف خیار عتق کے کہ امیں مختلقہ خود نکاح کو فسخ کر سکتی ہے قضاء قاضی کی ضرورت نہیں۔ وجہ فرق سے پہلے یہ ذہن نشین کر لیجئے کہ اپنے اوپر سے ضرر کو دفع کرنے کیلئے قاضی کا فیصلہ شرط نہیں البتہ دوسرے پر الزام لگانے کیلئے قضاء قاضی شرط ہے کیونکہ الزام قاضی کا منصب ہے، عام لوگوں کا نہیں ۔ اب وجہ فرق سنئے. خیار بلوغ میں فسخ نکاح کسی ضرر خفی کو دفع کرنے کے لئے ہے اور وہ ہے خلل کا ممکن ہونا یہی وجہ ہے کہ خیار بلوغ بذکر اور مؤنث دونوں کو شامل ہے اور جب یہ دفع ضرر خفی کا دفع ہے تو اس کو الزام علی الغیر کے حکم میں بنا دیا جائے گا۔ یعنی جس نے نکاح کو فسخ کرنے کا ارادہ کیا گویا وہ دوسرے پر جس نے ولی بن کر نکاح کیا اس پر الزام لگا رہا ہے کہ میرا نکاح مناسب جگہ نہیں کیا اور جب یہ دفع الزام ہے اور الزام قاضی کا منصب ہے لہذا خیار بلوغ کی وجہ سے فسخ کو قضاء قاضی کے ساتھ شرط کر دیا گیا۔ اور خیار عتق ضرر جلی کو دفع کرنے کے لئے ہے اس لئے کہ باندی جب تک آزاد نہیں ہوئی تھی اس وقت تک اس کا شوہر دو طلاقوں کا مالک تھا اور جب آزاد ہوگئی تو اب تین طلاقوں کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ تو گویا معتقہ پر آزادی کی وجہ سے ملک کا اضافہ ہو گیا۔ اور چونکہ زیادتی ملک باندی پر ہوگی غلام پر نہیں اس لئے خیار عتق باندی کے ساتھ خاص ہے غلام کو خیار عتق حاصل نہیں ہو گا۔ اور جب خیار عتق کی وجہ سے فسخ میں صرف دفع ضرر ہے الزام کے معنی بالکل نہیں تو خیار عتق میں فسخ نکاح قضاء قاضی کا محتاج بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
Book of Nikah. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya volume four. And grandfather both have complete judgment and abundant compassion, so the marriage conducted by both will be binding. For example, if after puberty the father or grandfather married them with their consent, that marriage will be binding. If someone other than the father or grandfather performed the marriage, then both have an option: "And if someone other than the father or grandfather married her, then each of them has the option upon reaching puberty: if they wish they may uphold the marriage, and if they wish they may annul it. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: They have no option, drawing analogy with the father and grandfather. Their evidence is that the brother's relationship is deficient, and deficiency indicates lack of compassion, so defect may enter into the objectives, and rectification is possible through the option of attainment (khiyar al-bulugh). And the absolute answer regarding other than father and grandfather includes the mother and the judge, and that is the correct transmission due to deficiency of opinion in one and deficiency of compassion in the other, so they have the option, and qada (judge's decree) is required in it, contrary to the option of emancipation (khiyar al-'itq) because the annulment there is to repel a hidden harm which is the possibility of defect, and therefore it includes both male and female, so it is considered as imposing (ilzam) upon the other, so it requires qada. And khiyar al-'itq is to repel a manifest harm, which is the increase of ownership over her, and therefore it is specific to the female, so it is considered as repulsion (daf'), and repulsion does not require qada." Translation: And if the marriage of a minor boy and girl is performed by other than father and grandfather, then each of them has an option upon puberty, if they wish they may keep the marriage, and if they wish they may annul it, and this is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). And Abu Yusuf said: They do not have an option, drawing analogy upon father and grandfather. And the evidence of the two is that the brother's relationship is deficient, and deficiency of relationship indicates deficiency of compassion. So the occurrence of defect in the objectives is possible, and rectification is possible through khiyar al-bulugh. And the absolute ruling regarding other than father and grandfather includes the mother and the judge, and that is the correct transmission due to deficiency of opinion in one of them and deficiency of compassion in the other, so they have the option, and qada of the judge is required in khiyar al-bulugh, contrary to khiyar al-'itq because here it is to repel a hidden harm, and that hidden harm is the possibility of defect. And for this reason it includes both male and female, so it will be considered as imposing upon the other, thus it requires qada. And khiyar al-'itq is to repel a manifest harm, and that manifest harm is the increase of ownership over the freed slave woman, and for this reason it is specific to the female, so repulsion is considered, and repulsion does not require qada. Explanation: In this phrase, the issue of wilayat al-ijbar is explained. The issue is that if the marriage of a minor boy and girl is performed by someone other than the father and grandfather, then after puberty each of the minors has the option under khiyar al-bulugh to keep the marriage or annul it. This is the ruling according to the two. Imam Abu Yusuf said that the minors do not have khiyar al-bulugh. Imam Abu Yusuf draws an analogy between other than father and grandfather and the father and grandfather. That is, just as the marriage performed by the father and grandfather is binding and cannot be annulled after puberty, similarly the marriage performed by other than father and grandfather will also be binding, and after puberty the minors will not have the option to annul. The common factor between the analogized and the analogized upon is relationship. The conclusion is that according to Abu Yusuf, other than father and grandfather also have wilayat al-ilzam along with wilayat al-ijbar like the father and grandfather. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya volume four. Book of Nikah. The evidence of the two is that the relationship of someone other than the father and grandfather, for example a brother, is deficient compared to the relationship of the father and grandfather. And deficiency of relationship is evidence of deficiency of compassion. So due to deficiency of compassion, the occurrence of defect in the marriage performed by other than father and grandfather is possible. And rectification of the possibility of defect in the objectives of marriage that has arisen due to deficiency of compassion is possible through khiyar al-bulugh. So for this rectification, the minors have khiyar al-bulugh. And the marriage performed by other than father and grandfather will not be binding. The conclusion is that according to the two, other than father and grandfather have wilayat al-ijbar but not wilayat al-ilzam. The implication of the absolute answer is that the ruling includes the mother and the judge as well, meaning the mother and the judge also have wilayat al-ijbar but not wilayat al-ilzam, so their performed marriage is also not binding, rather after puberty the minors have the right to annul it under khiyar al-bulugh. This is the correct transmission, although there is a transmission from Abu Hanifa that if a judge marries an orphan girl, she does not have khiyar al-bulugh, rather the marriage is binding, and the reason is that the judge has established guardianship over both property and person, so his guardianship is equal in strength to that of the father and grandfather. The evidence of the correct transmission is that for wilayat al-ilzam two things are necessary: perfection of opinion and perfection of compassion. If both are found, then wilayat al-ilzam is established. And if only one of them is found, then only wilayat al-ijbar is established, not wilayat al-ilzam. Here it is the case because the mother has perfection of compassion but not perfection of opinion, and the judge has perfection of opinion but not perfection of compassion. So both have wilayat al-ijbar but not wilayat al-ilzam. Therefore their marriage is not binding, and the minors have the option to annul. The author of al-Hidayah says that if the marriage is annulled due to khiyar al-bulugh, then the qada of the judge is a condition in it, meaning that the mere statement of annulment by the minor is not sufficient; rather they must present the case in the judge's court, then the judge gives the ruling of annulment. Contrary to khiyar al-'itq, where the freed slave woman herself can annul the marriage without needing the judge's decree. Before explaining the difference, note that to repel harm from oneself, the judge's decree is not a condition; however, to impose (ilzam) on another, qada of the judge is a condition because imposing is the function of the judge, not of common people. Now hear the reason for the difference. In khiyar al-bulugh, the annulment of the marriage is to repel a hidden harm, and that is the possibility of defect. This is why khiyar al-bulugh includes both male and female. And when it is a repulsion of hidden harm, it is given the ruling of imposing (ilzam) on the other. That is, the one who intends to annul the marriage is as if he is imposing on the other who performed the marriage as guardian, saying that my marriage was not done in a suitable place. And since it is a repulsion that involves imposition, and imposition is the function of the judge, therefore the annulment due to khiyar al-bulugh is conditioned upon the judge's decree. And khiyar al-'itq is to repel a manifest harm, because when the slave woman was not free, her husband had ownership of two divorces, and when she became free, he would become owner of three divorces. So upon the freed slave woman, due to freedom, an increase of ownership occurred. And since the increase of ownership applies to the female slave, not the male slave, therefore khiyar al-'itq is specific to the female slave; the male slave does not have khiyar al-'itq. And since in khiyar al-'itq the annulment is merely repulsion of harm without any meaning of imposition, in khiyar al-'itq the annulment of marriage does not need the judge's decree. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya is an expansion on a ruling from al-Hidaya regarding khiyar al-bulugh (the option of puberty) for minors when their marriage is contracted by a guardian other than their father or paternal grandfather. It presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad on one side, and Imam Abu Yusuf on the other, and then discusses the requirement of a judge's decree for the exercise of this option, contrasting it with khiyar al-'itq (option of emancipation).

The ruling: If someone other than the father or grandfather (such as a brother, mother, or judge) marries a minor boy or girl, then upon reaching puberty, each minor has the option to either uphold the marriage or annul it. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn). Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that the marriage is binding and there is no option, drawing an analogy with the father and grandfather. The reasoning of the majority is that the relationship of other guardians (like a brother) is deficient compared to that of a father or grandfather, and deficiency in relationship indicates deficiency in compassion (shafaqah). Due to this deficiency, there is a possibility that the marriage was not in the minor's best interest, and the option at puberty allows rectification of any potential harm.

The passage then clarifies that this ruling applies to all guardians other than the father and grandfather, including the mother and the judge. The mother has perfect compassion but imperfect judgment, while the judge has perfect judgment but imperfect compassion. Therefore, both have the authority to contract the marriage (wilayat al-ijbar) but not the power to make it irrevocably binding (wilayat al-ilzam). Thus their contracted marriages are not automatically binding, and the minor retains the option.

A key discussion is whether the exercise of khiyar al-bulugh requires a judge's decree (qada). The text, following al-Hidayah, states that it does require qada, unlike khiyar al-'itq. The rationale is that khiyar al-bulugh involves repelling a hidden harm (daf' darar khafi), which implies an implicit imposition (ilzam) on the guardian who contracted the marriage. Since imposing something on another is the function of the judge, the minor cannot simply declare annulment; they must go to court. In contrast, khiyar al-'itq repels a manifest harm (darar jali), specifically the increase of the husband's power of divorce over a freed slave woman. Since this is purely a repulsion of harm from oneself without any implication of blaming the other party, no judge's decree is needed; the freed woman can annul the marriage herself.

The passage also notes a weaker transmission from Abu Hanifa that if a judge marries an orphan girl, the marriage is binding without option, because the judge's guardianship is comprehensive (over property and person), making him like a father. But the correct position is that the judge lacks perfect compassion, so his marriage is not binding.

Key Terms
خیار البلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option of a minor, upon reaching puberty, to either annul or uphold a marriage that was contracted for them by a guardian other than their father or grandfather.
ولایت اجبار (wilayat al-ijbar): The authority of a guardian to contract a marriage for a minor without the minor's consent, but the marriage may be subject to the minor's option upon puberty.
ولایت الزام (wilayat al-ilzam): The authority to make a marriage contract binding and irrevocable, so that neither party can annul it after puberty. This belongs only to the father and grandfather.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), which statement about a minor married by a brother is correct?
A) The minor has no option upon puberty.
B) The minor may annul the marriage without a judge.
C) The minor may annul the marriage upon puberty, but only with a judge's decree.
D) The marriage is invalid.

Key Takeaway
For non-father/grandfather guardians, the marriage is valid but the minor retains the option to annul at puberty due to the possibility of deficient compassion.

Nikah — Marriage
advanced
10 min
The Requirement of Qada: Distinguishing Khiyar al-Bulugh from Khiyar al-'Itq
Explains why a judge's decree is needed for khiyar al-bulugh but not for khiyar al-'itq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the legal distinction between khiyar al-bulugh and khiyar al-'itq regarding the need for a judge's decree, and state the underlying rationale of hidden vs. manifest harm.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-bulugh requires a judge because annulment implies blaming the guardian; khiyar al-'itq is purely defensive and needs no qada.

Once we know that a minor can annul a marriage via khiyar al-bulugh, an important procedural question arises: can the minor simply declare annulment, or must they go to court? The Hanafi answer is that a judge's decree is required. This contrasts with khiyar al-'itq (the option of a freed slave woman), which can be exercised without any court involvement. This lesson explores the rationale behind this difference, focusing on the nature of the harm being repelled and the concept of imposition (ilzam) vs. repulsion (daf').

Guided Path
1
Identify the two khiyars
Khiyar al-bulugh: option for a minor married by a non-father/grandfather guardian. Khiyar al-'itq: option for a female slave upon being freed to annul her marriage due to the increase in the husband's power of divorce.
Both allow annulment, but the procedure differs.
2
State the ruling on qada
Khiyar al-bulugh requires a judge's decree (qada). Khiyar al-'itq does not.
This is the established Hanafi position.
3
Analyze the type of harm
Khiyar al-bulugh repels a hidden harm (daf' darar khafi): the possibility of defect in the guardian's choice. Khiyar al-'itq repels a manifest harm (darar jali): the increase in the husband's power of divorce from two to three.
Hidden harm is not apparent; manifest harm is obvious.
4
Apply the principle of ilzam vs. daf'
Repelling hidden harm involves an implicit imposition (ilzam) on the guardian, implying that the guardian's action was flawed. Imposition is the function of the judge. Repelling manifest harm is pure repulsion (daf') of harm from oneself, which any person can do without a judge.
Ilzam requires judicial authority; daf' is individual.
5
Conclude the practical difference
A minor must go to court to annul via khiyar al-bulugh. A freed slave woman can annul her marriage unilaterally via khiyar al-'itq.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم

اور دادا دونوں کامل رائے اور بھر پور شفقت رکھتے ہیں اس لئے کہ دونوں کا کیا ہوا نکاح لازم ہوگا جیسے اگر بالغ ہونے کے بعد باپ یا دادا نے ان دونوں کی رضا مندی سے نکاح کیا ہے تو وہ نکاح لازم ہوگا۔
اگر باپ اور داد کے علاوہ کسی نے نکاح کرایا تو دونوں کو جیار ہے
و ان زوجها غير الاب والجد فلكل واحد منهما الخيار اذا بلغ ان شاء اقام على النكاح وان شاء فسخ وهذا عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وقال ابويوسف لاخيار لهما اعتبارا بالاب والجد ولهما ان قرابة الاخ ناقصة والنقصان يشعر بقصور الشفقة فيتطرق الخلل الى المقاصد عسى والتدارک ممکن بخيار الادراك واطلاق الجواب في غير الاب والجديتناول الام والقاضى وهو الصحيح من الرواية لقصور الراى فى احدهما ونقصان الشفقة فى الآخر فيتخير ويشترط فيه القضاء بخلاف خيار العتق لان الفسخ هنالد فع ضرر محفى وهو تمكن الخلل ولهذا يشمل الذكر والانثى فجعل الزامافي حق الآخر فيفتقر الى القضاء وخيار العتق لدفع ضرر جلى و هو زيادة الملك عليها ولهذا يختص بالانثى فاعتبر دفعا و الدفع لا يفتقر الى القضاء

ترجمہ اور اگر نکاح کیا صغیر اور صغیرہ کا باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ نے تو ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے لئے خیار ہے جب بالغ ہو جائے جی چاہے نکاح کو باقی رکھے اور جی چاہے فسخ کر دے اور یہ طرفین کے نزدیک ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ ان دونوں کو خیار نہیں قیاس کرتے ہوئے باپ اور دادا پر۔ اور ان دونوں کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بھائی کی قرابت ناقص ہے اور نقصان قرابت خبر دیتا ہے قصور شفقت کی۔ پس مقاصد میں خلل کا واقع ہونا ممکن ہے اور تلافی ممکن ہے خیار بلوغ سے اور باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ میں حکم کا مطلق ہونا شامل ہے ماں اور قاضی کو ۔ اور یہ صحیح روایت ہے رائے کے ناقص ہونے کی وجہ سے ان دونوں میں سے ایک مین اور نقصان شفقت دوسرے میں لہذا اختیار ہیگا اور شرط لگائی گئی خیار بلوغ میں قضاء قاضی کی ۔ بخلاف خیار عتق کے اس لئے کہ یہاں فتح ضرر خفی کو دور کرنے کیلئے ہے اور وہ ضرر خفی خلل کا ممکن ہونا ہے۔ اور اسی وجہ سے شامل ہوگا ذکر اور مؤنث دونوں کو پس دوسرے کے حق میں الزام قرار دیا جائے گا لہذا قضاء کا محتاج ہوگا اور خیار عتق ضرر جلی کو دور کرنے کیلئے ہے اور وہ ضرر جلی معتقہ پر ملک کا زیادہ ہونا ہے اور اسی وجہ سے محفوظ ہوگا مونث کے ساتھ پس اعتبار کیا جائے گا دفع اور دفع قضا کامحتاج نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں ولایت اجبار پر تفریح بیان کی ہے۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر صغیر اور صغیرہ کا نکاح باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ نے کیا تو بالغ ہونے کے بعد صغیرین میں سے ہر ایک کو خیار بلوغ کے تحت نکاح کو باقی رکھنے اور نسخ کر دینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ یہ حکم طرفین کے نزدیک ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ صغیرین کو خیار بلوغ حاصل نہیں ہوگا ۔ امام ابو یوسف غیراب اور جد کو قیاس کرتے ہیں اب اور جد پر۔ یعنی جس طرح باپ اور دادا کا کیا ہوا نکاح لازم ہوتا ہے بالغ ہونے کے بعد اس کو فسخ نہیں کیا جا سکتا اسی طرح غیر باپ اور دادا کا کیا ہوا نکاح بھی لازم ہو گا۔ بالغ ہونے کے بعد صغیرین کو فسخ کا اختیار نہیں ہو گا۔ مقیس اور مقیس علیہ کے درمیان جامع قرابت ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک باپ دادا کی طرح غیر باپ اور غیر دادا کو بھی ولایت اجبار کے ساتھ ولایت الزام حاصل ہوگی۔

كتاب النكاح

طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ مثلاً بھائی کی قرابت باپ دادا کی قرابت سے ناقص ہے۔ اور نقصان قرابت دلیل ہے نقصان شفقت کی. پس نقصان شفقت کی وجہ سے باپ دادا کے علاوہ کے کئے ہوئے نکاح میں خلل کا واقع ہو نا ممکن ہے۔ اور نقصان شفقت کی وجہ سے مقاصد نکاح میں جو خلل کا امکان پیدا ہو گیا ہے خیار بلوغ کے ذریعہ اس کی تلافی بھی ممکن ہے۔ پس اس خلل کی تلافی کے لئے صغیرین کو خیار بلوغ حاصل ہوگا۔ اور باپ دادا کے علاوہ کا کیا ہوا نکاح لازم نہیں ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ طرفین کے نزدیک غیراب اور غیر جد کو ولایت اجبار تو حاصل ہے لیکن ولایت الزام حاصل نہیں ۔
واطلاق الجواب کا منشاء یہ ہے کہ حکم کا اطلاق باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ میں ماں اور قاضی کو بھی شامل ہے مطلب یہ ہے کہ ماں اور قاضی کو بھی ولایت اجبار حاصل ہے ولایت الزام حاصل نہیں لہذا ان کا کیا ہوا نکاح بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا بلکہ بالغ ہونے کے بعد صغیرین کو خیار بلوغ کے تحت فسخ کر دینے کا حق ہے صحیح روایت یہی ہے اگر چہ ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ قاضی نے اگر کسی یتیمہ کا نکاح کر دیا تو اس کو خیار بلوغ حاصل نہیں ہوگا بلکہ نکاح لازم ہوگا اور وجہ یہ ہے کہ قاضی کے لئے مال اور نفس دونوں میں ولایت نامہ ثابت ہے لہذا قاضی کی ولایت قوۃ میں باپ اور دادا کی ولایت کے برابر ہوگی۔
روایت صحیحہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ولایت الزام کے لئے دو چیزیں ضروری ہیں کمال رائے اور کمال شفقت اگر یہ دونوں چیزیں پائی یہ ہیں اور گئیں تو ولایت الزام حاصل ہوگی ۔ اور اگر دونوں میں سے ایک چیز پائی گئی تو صرف ولایت اجبار حاصل ہوگی۔ ولایت الزام نہیں۔ یہاں یہی بات ہے کیونکہ ماں میں کمال شفقت ہے کمال رائے نہیں ، اور قاضی میں کمال رائے ہے کمال شفقت نہیں ۔ پس ان دونوں کو ولایت اجبار تو حاصل ہوگی ولایت الزام نہیں۔ لہذا ان دونوں کا کیا ہوا نکاح لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ اور صغیر میں کو فسخ کر دینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ خیار بلوغ کی وجہ سے اگر نکاح فسخ کیا گیا تو اسمیں قضاء قاضی شرط ہے یعینی صغیرین سے کسی ایک کا فسخ کہنا کافی نہیں ہوگا ، بلکہ قاضی کی عدالت میں مقدمہ پیش کریں۔ پھر قاضی فسخ نکاح کا حکم دے برخلاف خیار عتق کے کہ امیں مختلقہ خود نکاح کو فسخ کر سکتی ہے قضاء قاضی کی ضرورت نہیں۔ وجہ فرق سے پہلے یہ ذہن نشین کر لیجئے کہ اپنے اوپر سے ضرر کو دفع کرنے کیلئے قاضی کا فیصلہ شرط نہیں البتہ دوسرے پر الزام لگانے کیلئے قضاء قاضی شرط ہے کیونکہ الزام قاضی کا منصب ہے، عام لوگوں کا نہیں ۔ اب وجہ فرق سنئے. خیار بلوغ میں فسخ نکاح کسی ضرر خفی کو دفع کرنے کے لئے ہے اور وہ ہے خلل کا ممکن ہونا یہی وجہ ہے کہ خیار بلوغ بذکر اور مؤنث دونوں کو شامل ہے اور جب یہ دفع ضرر خفی کا دفع ہے تو اس کو الزام علی الغیر کے حکم میں بنا دیا جائے گا۔ یعنی جس نے نکاح کو فسخ کرنے کا ارادہ کیا گویا وہ دوسرے پر جس نے ولی بن کر نکاح کیا اس پر الزام لگا رہا ہے کہ میرا نکاح مناسب جگہ نہیں کیا اور جب یہ دفع الزام ہے اور الزام قاضی کا منصب ہے لہذا خیار بلوغ کی وجہ سے فسخ کو قضاء قاضی کے ساتھ شرط کر دیا گیا۔ اور خیار عتق ضرر جلی کو دفع کرنے کے لئے ہے اس لئے کہ باندی جب تک آزاد نہیں ہوئی تھی اس وقت تک اس کا شوہر دو طلاقوں کا مالک تھا اور جب آزاد ہوگئی تو اب تین طلاقوں کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ تو گویا معتقہ پر آزادی کی وجہ سے ملک کا اضافہ ہو گیا۔ اور چونکہ زیادتی ملک باندی پر ہوگی غلام پر نہیں اس لئے خیار عتق باندی کے ساتھ خاص ہے غلام کو خیار عتق حاصل نہیں ہو گا۔ اور جب خیار عتق کی وجہ سے فسخ میں صرف دفع ضرر ہے الزام کے معنی بالکل نہیں تو خیار عتق میں فسخ نکاح قضاء قاضی کا محتاج بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
Book of Nikah. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya volume four. And grandfather both have complete judgment and abundant compassion, so the marriage conducted by both will be binding. For example, if after puberty the father or grandfather married them with their consent, that marriage will be binding. If someone other than the father or grandfather performed the marriage, then both have an option: "And if someone other than the father or grandfather married her, then each of them has the option upon reaching puberty: if they wish they may uphold the marriage, and if they wish they may annul it. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: They have no option, drawing analogy with the father and grandfather. Their evidence is that the brother's relationship is deficient, and deficiency indicates lack of compassion, so defect may enter into the objectives, and rectification is possible through the option of attainment (khiyar al-bulugh). And the absolute answer regarding other than father and grandfather includes the mother and the judge, and that is the correct transmission due to deficiency of opinion in one and deficiency of compassion in the other, so they have the option, and qada (judge's decree) is required in it, contrary to the option of emancipation (khiyar al-'itq) because the annulment there is to repel a hidden harm which is the possibility of defect, and therefore it includes both male and female, so it is considered as imposing (ilzam) upon the other, so it requires qada. And khiyar al-'itq is to repel a manifest harm, which is the increase of ownership over her, and therefore it is specific to the female, so it is considered as repulsion (daf'), and repulsion does not require qada." Translation: And if the marriage of a minor boy and girl is performed by other than father and grandfather, then each of them has an option upon puberty, if they wish they may keep the marriage, and if they wish they may annul it, and this is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). And Abu Yusuf said: They do not have an option, drawing analogy upon father and grandfather. And the evidence of the two is that the brother's relationship is deficient, and deficiency of relationship indicates deficiency of compassion. So the occurrence of defect in the objectives is possible, and rectification is possible through khiyar al-bulugh. And the absolute ruling regarding other than father and grandfather includes the mother and the judge, and that is the correct transmission due to deficiency of opinion in one of them and deficiency of compassion in the other, so they have the option, and qada of the judge is required in khiyar al-bulugh, contrary to khiyar al-'itq because here it is to repel a hidden harm, and that hidden harm is the possibility of defect. And for this reason it includes both male and female, so it will be considered as imposing upon the other, thus it requires qada. And khiyar al-'itq is to repel a manifest harm, and that manifest harm is the increase of ownership over the freed slave woman, and for this reason it is specific to the female, so repulsion is considered, and repulsion does not require qada. Explanation: In this phrase, the issue of wilayat al-ijbar is explained. The issue is that if the marriage of a minor boy and girl is performed by someone other than the father and grandfather, then after puberty each of the minors has the option under khiyar al-bulugh to keep the marriage or annul it. This is the ruling according to the two. Imam Abu Yusuf said that the minors do not have khiyar al-bulugh. Imam Abu Yusuf draws an analogy between other than father and grandfather and the father and grandfather. That is, just as the marriage performed by the father and grandfather is binding and cannot be annulled after puberty, similarly the marriage performed by other than father and grandfather will also be binding, and after puberty the minors will not have the option to annul. The common factor between the analogized and the analogized upon is relationship. The conclusion is that according to Abu Yusuf, other than father and grandfather also have wilayat al-ilzam along with wilayat al-ijbar like the father and grandfather. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya volume four. Book of Nikah. The evidence of the two is that the relationship of someone other than the father and grandfather, for example a brother, is deficient compared to the relationship of the father and grandfather. And deficiency of relationship is evidence of deficiency of compassion. So due to deficiency of compassion, the occurrence of defect in the marriage performed by other than father and grandfather is possible. And rectification of the possibility of defect in the objectives of marriage that has arisen due to deficiency of compassion is possible through khiyar al-bulugh. So for this rectification, the minors have khiyar al-bulugh. And the marriage performed by other than father and grandfather will not be binding. The conclusion is that according to the two, other than father and grandfather have wilayat al-ijbar but not wilayat al-ilzam. The implication of the absolute answer is that the ruling includes the mother and the judge as well, meaning the mother and the judge also have wilayat al-ijbar but not wilayat al-ilzam, so their performed marriage is also not binding, rather after puberty the minors have the right to annul it under khiyar al-bulugh. This is the correct transmission, although there is a transmission from Abu Hanifa that if a judge marries an orphan girl, she does not have khiyar al-bulugh, rather the marriage is binding, and the reason is that the judge has established guardianship over both property and person, so his guardianship is equal in strength to that of the father and grandfather. The evidence of the correct transmission is that for wilayat al-ilzam two things are necessary: perfection of opinion and perfection of compassion. If both are found, then wilayat al-ilzam is established. And if only one of them is found, then only wilayat al-ijbar is established, not wilayat al-ilzam. Here it is the case because the mother has perfection of compassion but not perfection of opinion, and the judge has perfection of opinion but not perfection of compassion. So both have wilayat al-ijbar but not wilayat al-ilzam. Therefore their marriage is not binding, and the minors have the option to annul. The author of al-Hidayah says that if the marriage is annulled due to khiyar al-bulugh, then the qada of the judge is a condition in it, meaning that the mere statement of annulment by the minor is not sufficient; rather they must present the case in the judge's court, then the judge gives the ruling of annulment. Contrary to khiyar al-'itq, where the freed slave woman herself can annul the marriage without needing the judge's decree. Before explaining the difference, note that to repel harm from oneself, the judge's decree is not a condition; however, to impose (ilzam) on another, qada of the judge is a condition because imposing is the function of the judge, not of common people. Now hear the reason for the difference. In khiyar al-bulugh, the annulment of the marriage is to repel a hidden harm, and that is the possibility of defect. This is why khiyar al-bulugh includes both male and female. And when it is a repulsion of hidden harm, it is given the ruling of imposing (ilzam) on the other. That is, the one who intends to annul the marriage is as if he is imposing on the other who performed the marriage as guardian, saying that my marriage was not done in a suitable place. And since it is a repulsion that involves imposition, and imposition is the function of the judge, therefore the annulment due to khiyar al-bulugh is conditioned upon the judge's decree. And khiyar al-'itq is to repel a manifest harm, because when the slave woman was not free, her husband had ownership of two divorces, and when she became free, he would become owner of three divorces. So upon the freed slave woman, due to freedom, an increase of ownership occurred. And since the increase of ownership applies to the female slave, not the male slave, therefore khiyar al-'itq is specific to the female slave; the male slave does not have khiyar al-'itq. And since in khiyar al-'itq the annulment is merely repulsion of harm without any meaning of imposition, in khiyar al-'itq the annulment of marriage does not need the judge's decree. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya is an expansion on a ruling from al-Hidaya regarding khiyar al-bulugh (the option of puberty) for minors when their marriage is contracted by a guardian other than their father or paternal grandfather. It presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad on one side, and Imam Abu Yusuf on the other, and then discusses the requirement of a judge's decree for the exercise of this option, contrasting it with khiyar al-'itq (option of emancipation).

The ruling: If someone other than the father or grandfather (such as a brother, mother, or judge) marries a minor boy or girl, then upon reaching puberty, each minor has the option to either uphold the marriage or annul it. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn). Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that the marriage is binding and there is no option, drawing an analogy with the father and grandfather. The reasoning of the majority is that the relationship of other guardians (like a brother) is deficient compared to that of a father or grandfather, and deficiency in relationship indicates deficiency in compassion (shafaqah). Due to this deficiency, there is a possibility that the marriage was not in the minor's best interest, and the option at puberty allows rectification of any potential harm.

The passage then clarifies that this ruling applies to all guardians other than the father and grandfather, including the mother and the judge. The mother has perfect compassion but imperfect judgment, while the judge has perfect judgment but imperfect compassion. Therefore, both have the authority to contract the marriage (wilayat al-ijbar) but not the power to make it irrevocably binding (wilayat al-ilzam). Thus their contracted marriages are not automatically binding, and the minor retains the option.

A key discussion is whether the exercise of khiyar al-bulugh requires a judge's decree (qada). The text, following al-Hidayah, states that it does require qada, unlike khiyar al-'itq. The rationale is that khiyar al-bulugh involves repelling a hidden harm (daf' darar khafi), which implies an implicit imposition (ilzam) on the guardian who contracted the marriage. Since imposing something on another is the function of the judge, the minor cannot simply declare annulment; they must go to court. In contrast, khiyar al-'itq repels a manifest harm (darar jali), specifically the increase of the husband's power of divorce over a freed slave woman. Since this is purely a repulsion of harm from oneself without any implication of blaming the other party, no judge's decree is needed; the freed woman can annul the marriage herself.

The passage also notes a weaker transmission from Abu Hanifa that if a judge marries an orphan girl, the marriage is binding without option, because the judge's guardianship is comprehensive (over property and person), making him like a father. But the correct position is that the judge lacks perfect compassion, so his marriage is not binding.

Key Terms
خیار البلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option of a minor, upon reaching puberty, to annul or uphold a marriage contracted by a non-father/grandfather guardian.
خیار العتق (khiyar al-'itq): The option of a freed slave woman to annul her existing marriage due to increase in the husband's power of divorce.
قضاء (qada): A judge's decree or court order required for certain legal annulments.
ضرر خفی (darar khafi): Hidden harm – the possibility of defect in the guardian's choice, which is not immediately apparent.
ضرر جلی (darar jali): Manifest harm – the increase in the husband's power of divorce after emancipation, which is obvious.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does khiyar al-bulugh require a judge's decree while khiyar al-'itq does not?
A) Khiyar al-bulugh is for minors, and minors cannot act without a guardian.
B) Khiyar al-bulugh repels a hidden harm that involves implicit blame of another, requiring a judge's authoritative determination.
C) Khiyar al-'itq requires a judge but the text says otherwise.
D) There is no difference; both require qada.

Key Takeaway
The need for a judge in khiyar al-bulugh stems from the nature of the harm being hidden and the annulment implicating the guardian, whereas khiyar al-'itq is a straightforward defensive action against manifest harm.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Khiyar al-Bulugh: Non-Binding Marriages by Non-Father Guardians
Intra-Hanafi dispute on binding nature of marriage by non-father guardians

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on marriage by non-father guardians, identify the conditions for binding marriage (wilayat ilzam), and apply the distinction between wilayat ijbar and wilayat ilzam in concrete scenarios.

Core Idea
Marriage by non-father guardians is valid but not binding; the minor retains khiyar al-bulugh.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute: is a marriage contracted by a guardian other than the father or grandfather binding upon the minor? The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it is not binding due to deficiency in affection, while a narration from Abu Hanifa suggests the qadi's marriage is binding. The correct view establishes that wilayat ilzam requires both perfect judgment and perfect affection—qualities that mother and qadi lack respectively. We will also explore the procedural requirement for annulment, which distinguishes khiyar al-bulugh from the option of emancipation (khiyar al-'itq).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of the Sahibayn (Zahir al-Riwayah): marriage by a guardian other than father or grandfather is valid (sahih) but non-binding (ghayr lazim). The minor has khiyar al-bulugh upon reaching puberty.
This applies to all non-father guardians: brother, mother, qadi, etc.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note the opposing view: Abu Hanifa (in one narration) holds that the qadi's marriage is binding because the qadi has comprehensive authority over both property and person, similar to the father.
This is a weak (marjuh) narration; the sahih riwayah is the Sahibayn's.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent's dalil: the qadi's authority (wilayah) is universal, covering wealth and person, so his marriage should be as binding as the father's.
This is a rational analogy (qiyas) based on the scope of authority.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Sahibayn respond that wilayat ilzam (binding authority) requires two conditions: perfection of judgment (kamal al-ra'y) and perfection of affection (kamal al-shafaqah). The mother has affection but lacks judgment; the qadi has judgment but lacks affection. Therefore, neither has wilayat ilzam.
Thus, the qadi's marriage is also non-binding. The criterion is the combination, not just authority.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: If father/grandfather marries, no khiyar; if mother/qadi marries, khiyar exists. Also, annulment of khiyar al-bulugh requires a qadi's judgment, whereas khiyar al-'itq does not.
The need for qadi arises because annulment implies a claim against the guardian.

The proof of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that the relationship of other than father and grandfather, e.g. brother, is deficient compared to father and grandfather. And deficiency of relationship is evidence of deficiency of affection. So due to deficiency of affection, it is possible that a defect occurs in the marriage contracted by other than father and grandfather. And due to the possibility of defect in the objectives of marriage, it is possible to compensate for it through the option of puberty. So for compensation of this defect, minors will have the option of puberty. And the marriage done by other than father and grandfather will not be binding. In summary, according to the two, other than father and grandfather have wilayat ijbar (authority of compulsion) but do not have wilayat ilzam (authority of imposition).
And the purport of the absolute answer is that the ruling includes mother and qadi as well in the category of other than father and grandfather. Meaning that mother and qadi also have wilayat ijbar, not wilayat ilzam. Hence their marriage is also not binding; rather after reaching puberty, minors have the right to annul under the option of puberty. This is the correct narration, although there is a narration from Abu Hanifa that if a qadi marries an orphan girl, she does not have the option of puberty; rather the marriage is binding, and the reason is that the qadi has established authority over both property and person, so the qadi's authority is equivalent in strength to that of father and grandfather.
The proof of the correct narration is that for wilayat ilzam two things are necessary: perfection of opinion and perfection of affection. If both exist, then wilayat ilzam is established. And if only one exists, then only wilayat ijbar is established, not wilayat ilzam. Here is the case: the mother has perfection of affection but not perfection of opinion, and the qadi has perfection of opinion but not perfection of affection. So both will have wilayat ijbar but not wilayat ilzam. Therefore their marriage is not binding, and the minor will have the option to annul. The author of Hidayah states that if the marriage is annulled due to the option of puberty, then the judgment of a qadi is required, i.e., the mere statement of the minor is not sufficient; rather the case must be presented to the court, then the qadi gives the verdict of annulment. Contrary to the option of emancipation ('itq), where the freed slave woman can herself annul the marriage without needing a qadi's decision. Before explaining the difference, note: for repelling harm from oneself, a qadi's decision is not required; but for imposing a claim on another, a qadi's decision is required because imposing is the office of the qadi, not of common people. Now hear the reason for the difference. In the option of puberty, the annulment is for repelling a hidden harm, which is the possibility of a defect. This is why the option of puberty includes both free male and female. And since it is repelling a hidden harm, it is treated as an imposition against another, i.e., the one who intends to annul the marriage is essentially imposing a claim on the one who acted as guardian, saying he did not marry her appropriately. Since it is an imposition, and imposition is the office of the qadi, therefore the option of puberty is conditioned upon the qadi's judgment. And the option of emancipation is for repelling an apparent harm, because when the slave woman was a slave, her husband owned two divorces, and when she became free, he would own three divorces, so freedom increases her ownership rights. And since the increase of ownership occurs for the female slave, not the male slave, the option of emancipation is specific to the female slave; the male slave does not have the option of emancipation. And since in annulment due to the option of emancipation there is only repelling harm and no sense of imposition, therefore annulment in the option of emancipation does not require a qadi's judgment. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the binding nature of marriages contracted by guardians other than the father or grandfather. The text begins with the position of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad), who argue that such marriages are not binding (ghayr lazim) and that the minor has the option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh) to annul the marriage upon reaching majority. Their proof is rational: the affection of a brother or other relative is deficient compared to that of a father or grandfather, which may lead to a defect in the marriage. This hidden defect can be compensated by granting the minor the right to annul. Thus, such guardians have wilayat ijbar (authority to compel the marriage) but not wilayat ilzam (authority to make it irrevocably binding). The text then extends this ruling to the mother and the qadi, stating that they too fall under this category. However, a narration from Abu Hanifa holds that the qadi's marriage is binding because his authority over both property and person is equivalent to that of the father. The text rejects this as the weaker view, preferring the Sahibayn's position. The correct view (sahih riwayah) is that wilayat ilzam requires two conditions: perfection of judgment (kamal al-ra'y) and perfection of affection (kamal al-shafaqah). The mother has affection but lacks judgment; the qadi has judgment but lacks affection. Therefore, neither has wilayat ilzam, and their marriages are not binding. The passage then discusses a practical difference between khiyar al-bulugh and khiyar al-'itq (option of emancipation). In khiyar al-bulugh, annulment requires a qadi's judgment because it involves an implicit claim (ilzam) against the guardian, which is the qadi's prerogative. In khiyar al-'itq, no such claim exists; the harm (increase in the husband's power of divorce) is apparent and only concerns the woman herself, so she can annul without a qadi. This distinction is crucial for understanding when judicial intervention is necessary. The passage thus clarifies the limits of guardians' authority and the scope of the minor's right to annul.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option granted to a minor who was married by a guardian other than father or grandfather to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty.
ولایت اجبار (wilayat ijbar): Authority to compel the minor into marriage without their consent, held by certain guardians like father, grandfather, mother, and qadi in some cases.
ولایت الزام (wilayat ilzam): Authority to make the marriage irrevocably binding such that the minor has no option to annul upon puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because they lack any authority to marry the minor.
B) Because they lack either perfect judgment or perfect affection, which are both required for binding marriage.
C) Because the minor must always consent regardless of the guardian.
D) Because the marriage is invalid (fasid).

Key Takeaway
A minor married by a guardian other than father or grandfather retains the option of puberty to annul, because wilayat ilzam requires both complete judgment and complete affection.

Effect of Silence After Knowledge in Khiyar al-Bulugh
Ruling on whether silence after knowledge constitutes consent in khiyar al-bulugh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between knowledge of the marriage and knowledge of the option, and apply the Hanafi ruling for khiyar al-bulugh when the minor remains silent after puberty.

Core Idea
For free women, silence after knowing the marriage is consent, even if ignorant of the option, due to access to knowledge in Dar al-Islam.

This passage elaborates on the conditions for khiyar al-bulugh, specifically the effect of silence after attaining puberty. It is a ruling from the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad). The key distinction is between knowledge of the marriage and knowledge of the option of puberty. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the rule correctly in real cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the ruling
The subject is a minor girl who reaches puberty and knows of her marriage. The ruling is that her silence is considered consent (rida), making the marriage binding.
This is the position of the Sahibayn, the relied-upon view in the Hidayah.
2
Distinguish the two types of knowledge
The text distinguishes between knowledge of the marriage (asl al-nikah) and knowledge of the option of puberty (al-khiyar). The condition for consent is only knowledge of the marriage.
Knowledge of the option is not required for free women in Dar al-Islam.
3
Analyze the rationale for not requiring knowledge of the option
Dar al-Islam is a land of knowledge, and free women have the opportunity to learn Islamic rulings. Their ignorance of the option is therefore not excusable.
This is a rational proof (qiyas khafi/istihsan).
4
Contrast with the freed slave woman (mu'taqah)
A freed slave woman is excused for ignorance of her option (khiyar al-'itq) because as a slave she was occupied with service and could not learn. Her silence after freedom is not consent.
The exception highlights the 'illa: ability to pursue religious knowledge.
5
Conclude the effective cause ('illa)
The effective cause for excusing ignorance is the inability to learn. Free women in Dar al-Islam are expected to learn, so their ignorance is not excused; slave women are excused because they lack opportunity.
This 'illa governs the distinction between the two cases.

ہو جائے اصل نکاح کے علم کی شرط لگائی ہے کیونکہ وہ تصرف پر قادر نہیں ہوگی مگر علم بالنکاح سے اور ولی تنہا نکاح کر سکتا ہے۔ پس جہل کی وجہ سے صغیرہ معذور ہوگی ، اور خیار کے علم کی شرط نہیں لگائی اس لئے کہ وہ احکام شرع کی معرفت کے لئے اپنے آپ کو فارغ کر سکتی ہے۔ اور دارالاسلام واعلم ہے پس جہل بالخیار کی وجہ سے معذور نہیں ہوگی بر خلاف معتقہ کے اس لئے کہ باندی احکام شرع کے لئے فارغ نہیں۔ پس جہل بثبوت الخیار کی وجہ سے معذور ہوگی ۔ تشریح طرفین کے نزدیک ماقبل کے مسئلہ پر تفریح ہے۔ صورت یہ ہے کہ صغیرہ کو پہلے سے یہ علم تھا کہ فلاں کے ساتھ میرا نکاح ہو چکا ہے۔ اب بالغ ہونے کے بعد اس صغیرہ نے خاموشی اختیار کی تو یہ خاموشی اس کی طرف سے رضامندی ہوگی اور اگر پہلے سے اصل نکاح کا علم نہیں تھا۔ اسی دوران بالغ ہو گئی تو اس کو اس وقت تک اختیار حاصل رہے گا جب تک کہ اصل نکاح کا علم ہو۔ اور علم ہونے کے بعد اگر سکوت اختیار کیا تو رضا مندی شمار ہوگی ۔ حاصل یہ کہ طرفین نے حاصل نکاح سے واقف ہونے کی شرط لگائی ہے۔ اس لئے کہ ولی بغیر صغیرہ سے مشورہ کئے تنے تنہا نکاح کر سکتا ہے۔ اور صغیرہ خیار بلوغ کے تحت اس وقت تصرف پر قادر ہوگی جبکہ اسکو یہ معلوم ہو کہ میرا نکاح ہو چکا اس کے بغیر تصرف خیار پر قادر نہیں ہوسکتی اس لئے اس کو اصل نکاح سے جاہل رہنے کی صوررت میں منذ ور قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ اور کہا گیا کہ جب بھی اصل نکاح کا علم ہو گا خیار بلوغ حاصل ہوگا۔ علم بالنکاح کی شرط تو لگائی ہے مگر علم بالخیار کی شرط نہیں لگائی ۔ تفصیل یہ ہے کہ صغیرہ کو یہ تو معلوم ہے کہ میرا نکاح ہو چکا لیکن یہ معلوم نہیں کہ بالغ ہونے کے بعد شریعت نے مجھ کو خیار بلوغ کا حق دیا ہے یعنی یہ مسئلہ معلوم نہیں اب ایسی صورت میں اگر وہ بالغ ہونے کے بعد خاموش رہی تو نکاح لازم ہو جائیگا۔ در انحالیکہ اس کو خیار بلوغ کا علم نہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ دارالاسلام دارالعلم ہے۔ پڑھنے پڑھانے کے مواقع بھی ہیں۔ آزاد ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ صغیرہ بھی احکام شرع کو جانے اور سیکھنے کیلئے فارغ تھی ۔ لہذا اس کا جہل معتبر نہیں ہوگا اور ہم اس کو معذور نہیں سمجھیں گے۔ اس کے برخلاف معتقہ کہ آزاد ہونے کے بعد اسکو یہ مسئلہ معلوم نہیں کہ مجھ کو خیار عتق کے تحت نکاح فسخ کر دینے کا حق ہے۔ پس آزاد ہونے کے بعد معتقہ کا سکوت رضا مندی نہیں ہوگا، بلکہ معلوم ہونے تک خیار معتق باقی رہے گا۔ وجہ یہ ہے که باندی مولی کی خدمت میں مشغول ہونے کی وجہ سے احکام شرع سیکھنے کیلئے اپنا وقت فارغ نہیں کر سکتی تھی اسلئے باندی کو خیار عشق سے ناواقف رہنے میں معذور سمجھا جائے گا۔
According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): When the minor girl reaches puberty and she knows about the marriage and remains silent, then it is consent. And if she did not know about the marriage, she has the option until she knows and then remains silent. Knowledge of the original marriage is a condition because she cannot exercise the option except with knowledge of the marriage, and the guardian alone contracted it; so she is excused due to ignorance. And knowledge of the option is not made a condition because she can occupy herself with learning the rulings of Shariah, and Dar al-Islam is a land of knowledge, so she is not excused due to ignorance (of the option). Contrary to the case of the freed slave woman (mu'taqah), because the slave woman cannot occupy herself with learning, so she is excused due to ignorance of the existence of the option.
Translation: Then according to the two, when the minor girl reaches puberty and she is aware of the marriage, and she remains silent, then this is consent. And if she is not aware of the original marriage, she has the option until she knows and then remains silent. Knowledge of the original marriage is a condition because she cannot exercise the option except with knowledge of the marriage, and the guardian alone can contract the marriage. So due to ignorance, the minor is excused. And knowledge of the option is not made a condition because she can free herself for learning the rulings of Shariah, and Dar al-Islam is a land of knowledge, so she is not excused due to ignorance of the option. Contrary to the case of the freed slave woman, because the slave woman is not free for learning Shariah rulings, so she is excused due to ignorance of the existence of the option. Explanation: This is an elaboration of the previous issue according to the two. The scenario is that the minor girl knew beforehand that her marriage has been contracted with so-and-so. Now after reaching puberty, she remains silent; this silence is considered consent. And if she did not previously know about the original marriage, and in that state she reached puberty, then she will have the option until she knows about the original marriage. And after knowing, if she remains silent, it will be counted as consent. In summary, the two condition knowledge of the marriage because the guardian can contract the marriage without consulting the minor, and the minor can exercise the option of puberty only when she knows that her marriage has occurred. Without that, she cannot exercise the option. So she is considered excused in the case of ignorance of the marriage. And it is said that whenever she gains knowledge of the marriage, the option of puberty is established. The condition of knowledge of the marriage is set, but knowledge of the option is not set. The detail is that the minor knows that her marriage has occurred, but she does not know that after puberty, Shariah grants her the right of option of puberty, i.e., she does not know this ruling. In such a case, if she remains silent after puberty, the marriage becomes binding, despite her ignorance of the option of puberty. The proof is that Dar al-Islam is a land of knowledge. There are opportunities for learning. Being free, this minor is also free to learn and know the rulings of Shariah. Hence her ignorance is not considered valid, and we do not consider her excused. On the contrary, the freed slave woman: after freedom, she does not know this ruling that she has the right to annul the marriage under the option of emancipation. So after freedom, her silence is not consent; rather, the option of emancipation remains until she knows. The reason is that the slave woman, being occupied in the service of her master, could not free her time for learning Shariah rulings, so the slave woman is considered excused in her ignorance of the option of emancipation.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the conditions for khiyar al-bulugh, specifically the effect of silence after attaining puberty. It is a ruling from the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad). They state that if the minor girl becomes an adult and knows about the marriage, her silence is considered consent (rida), and the option is lost. If she did not know about the marriage, she retains the option until she learns of it and then remains silent. The key distinction is between knowledge of the marriage (al-'ilm bi asl al-nikah) and knowledge of the option of puberty (al-'ilm bi al-khiyar). The Sahibayn require knowledge of the marriage for the option to expire, but they do not require knowledge of the option itself. This is because the minor cannot be expected to know of the marriage without being informed, as the guardian acted alone. Once she knows, she can seek knowledge about her legal rights, and since Dar al-Islam is a place of learning, her ignorance of the option is not excused. In contrast, for a slave woman who is freed (khiyar al-'itq), her ignorance of the option is excused because as a slave she was occupied with service and could not learn. Therefore, her silence after freedom does not imply consent until she knows of her right. This lesson highlights that the legal reason ('illa) for excusing ignorance is the ability and opportunity to learn: free women in Muslim lands are expected to know basic fiqh rulings, while slaves are not.

Key Terms
معتقہ (mu'taqah): A female slave who has been freed, who retains the option of emancipation (khiyar al-'itq) to annul her marriage if she was married while a slave.
دار الاسلام (Dar al-Islam): A land where Islamic law prevails, and Muslims have the opportunity to learn religious rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Sahibayn consider the silence of a free minor girl after puberty as consent even if she is ignorant of the option of puberty?
A) Because she is expected to know all Islamic rulings by instinct.
B) Because Dar al-Islam is a land of knowledge, and she has the opportunity to learn, so her ignorance is not excused.
C) Because the guardian informed her of the option.
D) Because she is a slave and not expected to know.

Key Takeaway
A free woman's silence after knowledge of marriage is consent, regardless of ignorance of the option, because she has the opportunity to learn Islamic rulings; a slave woman is excused due to her inability to learn.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Sahibayn's Ruling on Khiyar al-Bulugh: Knowledge of Marriage as Condition for Consent
Explains conditions for minor girl's silence to be consent at puberty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Sahibayn's position on khiyar al-bulugh regarding the condition of knowledge of marriage and the excuse of ignorance of the option, and distinguish between the cases of a free minor girl and an emancipated slave girl.

Core Idea
Knowledge of marriage is necessary for silence to be consent; ignorance of the option is not excused for a free woman in Dar al-Islam.

In this lesson, we study the view of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn) on the minor girl's option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh). They introduce a crucial condition: the girl must know that she was married for her silence after puberty to count as consent. Additionally, they rule that once she knows she was married, her silence is binding even if she is unaware of her legal right to annul the marriage. This is because a free woman in Dar al-Islam has the means to learn the Shari'ah rulings. The ruling is contrasted with an emancipated slave girl, who is excused for ignorance of her option due to her previous servitude.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on khiyar al-bulugh according to Sahibayn
Read the first part of the passage: if a minor girl attains puberty and knows of the marriage, her silence is consent. If she does not know, she retains the option until she knows and then remains silent.
The phrase 'عندهما' indicates this is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, not Abu Hanifa.
2
Understand the condition of knowledge of the marriage
The passage states that knowledge of the original marriage (al-nikah) is required because the girl cannot exercise disposal (al-tasarruf) regarding the option without that knowledge. The guardian acted alone, so she is excused if ignorant of the marriage itself.
This condition parallels the initial marriage contract where a virgin's silence is consent only if she knows the proposal.
3
Understand why knowledge of the option is not required for a free girl
Once she knows of the marriage, her silence is consent even if she is unaware of the legal right to object (khiyar). The reason: she can free herself to learn the rulings of Shari'ah, and Dar al-Islam is a land of knowledge. Thus ignorance of the option is not excused.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that knowledge of the law is presumed in Dar al-Islam for free persons.
4
Compare with the case of an emancipated slave girl (mu'taqah)
The passage contrasts the free girl with an emancipated slave girl. The slave girl is excused for ignorance of the existence of khiyar al-'itq because she was occupied with service and could not learn the rulings. Her silence is not consent until she knows of the option.
The difference arises from the slave's inability to free herself to seek knowledge, not from her status after freedom.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of this intra-Hanafi dispute
According to Sahibayn, if a free minor girl attains puberty and does not know she was married, her silence is not consent and she retains the option. If she knows the marriage but not the option, silence is consent. For the slave girl, ignorance of the option excuses silence.
The practice consequence: the timing and conditions under which the marriage becomes binding differ between the views of Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa.

Source Text

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چهارم
طرفین کا نقطہ نظر
عندهما اذا بلغت الصغيرة وقد علمت بالنكاح فسكتت فهورضا وان لم تعلم بالنكاح فلها الخيار حتى تعلم فتسكت شرط العلم باصل النكاح لانها لا تتمكن من التصرف الابه والولى يتفرد به فعذرت بالجهل و لم يتشرط العلم بالخيار لانها تتفرغ لمعرفة احكام الشرع والدار دار العلم فلم تعذر بالجهل بخلاف المعتقة لان الامة لاتتفرغ لمعرفتها فعذرت بالجهل بثبوت الخيار

الخیار کی وجہ سے معذور ہوگی ۔ تشریح طرفین کے نزدیک ماقبل کے مسئلہ پر تفریح ہے۔ صورت یہ ہے کہ صغیرہ کو پہلے سے یہ علم تھا کہ فلاں کے ساتھ میرا نکاح ہو چکا ہے۔ اب بالغ ہونے کے بعد اس صغیرہ نے خاموشی اختیار کی تو یہ خاموشی اس کی طرف سے رضامندی ہوگی اور اگر پہلے سے اصل نکاح کا علم نہیں تھا۔ اسی دوران بالغ ہو گئی تو اس کو اس وقت تک اختیار حاصل رہے گا جب تک کہ اصل نکاح کا علم ہو۔ اور علم ہونے کے بعد اگر سکوت اختیار کیا تو رضا مندی شمار ہوگی ۔ حاصل یہ کہ طرفین نے حاصل نکاح سے واقف ہونے کی شرط لگائی ہے۔ اس لئے کہ ولی بغیر صغیرہ سے مشورہ کئے تنے تنہا نکاح کر سکتا ہے۔ اور صغیرہ خیار بلوغ کے تحت اس وقت تصرف پر قادر ہوگی جبکہ اسکو یہ معلوم ہو کہ میرا نکاح ہو چکا اس کے بغیر تصرف خیار پر قادر نہیں ہوسکتی اس لئے اس کو اصل نکاح سے جاہل رہنے کی صوررت میں منذ ور قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ اور کہا گیا کہ جب بھی اصل نکاح کا علم ہو گا خیار بلوغ حاصل ہوگا۔ علم بالنکاح کی شرط تو لگائی ہے مگر علم بالخیار کی شرط نہیں لگائی ۔ تفصیل یہ ہے کہ صغیرہ کو یہ تو معلوم ہے کہ میرا نکاح ہو چکا لیکن یہ معلوم نہیں کہ بالغ ہونے کے بعد شریعت نے مجھ کو خیار بلوغ کا حق دیا ہے یعنی یہ مسئلہ معلوم نہیں اب ایسی صورت میں اگر وہ بالغ ہونے کے بعد خاموش رہی تو نکاح لازم ہو جائیگا۔ در انحالیکہ اس کو خیار بلوغ کا علم نہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ دارالاسلام دارالعلم ہے۔ پڑھنے پڑھانے کے مواقع بھی ہیں۔ آزاد ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ صغیرہ بھی احکام شرع کو جانے اور سیکھنے کیلئے فارغ تھی ۔ لہذا اس کا جہل معتبر نہیں ہوگا اور ہم اس کو معذور نہیں سمجھیں گے۔ اس کے برخلاف معتقہ کہ آزاد ہونے کے بعد اسکو یہ مسئلہ معلوم نہیں کہ مجھ کو خیار عتق کے تحت نکاح فسخ کر دینے کا حق ہے۔ پس آزاد ہونے کے بعد معتقہ کا سکوت رضا مندی نہیں ہوگا، بلکہ معلوم ہونے تک خیار معتق باقی رہے گا۔ وجہ یہ ہے که باندی مولی کی خدمت میں مشغول ہونے کی وجہ سے احکام شرع سیکھنے کیلئے اپنا وقت فارغ نہیں کر سکتی تھی اسلئے باندی کو خیار عشق سے ناواقف رہنے میں معذور سمجھا جائے گا۔
According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): When a minor girl attains puberty and she knows of the marriage and remains silent, that is consent. If she does not know of the marriage, she has the option until she knows and then remains silent. Knowledge of the marriage itself is a condition because she cannot exercise disposal (of the option) except with that knowledge, and the guardian alone performs the marriage, so she is excused due to ignorance. Knowledge of the option itself is not required because she can devote herself to learning the rulings of Shari'ah, and Dar al-Islam is a place of knowledge, so she is not excused for ignorance of the option. Unlike an emancipated slave girl, because a slave girl cannot devote herself to that knowledge, so she is excused for ignorance of the existence of the option.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) regarding khiyar al-bulugh for a minor girl. They distinguish between knowledge of the marriage itself and knowledge of the option. If she knows she was married and remains silent after puberty, it is consent. If she did not know, she has the option until she learns. The reason: she cannot rationally reject a marriage she does not know about. However, once she knows, her silence is consent even if she does not know the legal right to object, because a free woman in Dar al-Islam is expected to learn such basic rulings. In contrast, a slave girl who is freed is excused for ignorance of khiyar al-‘itq because she was occupied with service. The comparison is made: the free minor girl's case is treated as similar to the initial marriage contract where silence of a virgin is consent, but the slave girl's case differs due to her circumstances.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option of a minor who was married by his/her guardian to annul or confirm the marriage upon attaining puberty.
سکوت (sukut): Silence after being asked about consent; for a virgin, it is considered consent in marriage matters.
معتقة (mu'taqah): A slave girl who is emancipated and has the option to annul her marriage upon freedom (khiyar al-'itq).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if a minor girl attains puberty and remains silent while knowing that she was married, what is the effect?
A) Her silence is not consent because she may not know her option.
B) Her silence is consent and the marriage becomes binding.
C) She still has the option until she explicitly says 'I consent'.
D) The marriage is invalid.

Key Takeaway
According to Sahibayn, a minor girl's silence after puberty constitutes consent only if she knew she was married; ignorance of the option is not excused for a free woman, but is excused for an emancipated slave.

Khiyar al-Bulugh: How Each Party's Option Is Extinguished
Ruling with proof: khiyar al-bulugh extinction rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which signs extinguish khiyar al-bulugh for a virgin, a boy, and a thayyib, and explain the underlying qiyas with the initial marriage contract.

Core Idea
A virgin's silence in khiyar al-bulugh is consent; a boy or thayyib must speak or act clearly.

Khiyar al-bulugh gives a minor who was married before puberty the option to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty. But how is this option lost? The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the person's status: a virgin's silence is taken as acceptance, while a boy or a non-virgin woman must explicitly consent. This lesson unpacks the rule and its analogy to the initial marriage contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories
The passage distinguishes three parties: a virgin girl (bikr), a boy (ghulam), and a non-virgin woman (thayyib). For each, the condition to nullify khiyar al-bulugh is different.
The thayyib here is a slave girl whose husband had intercourse before her puberty; the rule is the same as for a free thayyib.
2
Determine the nullifying act
For the virgin, silence alone extinguishes the option. For the boy and thayyib, they must say 'I consent' or do an act that clearly indicates consent, such as sending mahr or having intercourse.
The text says 'or something comes from him that is known to be consent' – this includes clear conduct.
3
Trace the qiyas (analogy)
The ruling is based on analogy with the initial marriage contract: when a guardian seeks permission, a virgin's silence is consent, but a thayyib must speak. The same logic applies to khiyar al-bulugh.
The illa (ratio legis) is the similarity of the situation – both involve a person with a right to consent or object in marriage.
4
Note the scope of the option
For the virgin, the option does not extend beyond the sitting (majlis) in which she attains puberty or learns of the marriage. Standing up nullifies it. For the boy and thayyib, standing does not nullify the option; it remains until they consent explicitly or leave? Actually, the text says it is not nullified by standing up (la yabtul bil-qiyam).
The exact duration for a boy/thayyib is not fully detailed here, but they are not bound by the sitting like the virgin.
5
Contrast with khiyar al-‛itq
The option upon emancipation (khiyar al-‛itq) is different: it is established by the master's act, so it requires explicit consent and is tied to the sitting, similar to khiyar al-mukhayyarah in sales.
This contrast helps understand the strength of the right: khiyar al-bulugh is a weaker right based on presumed defect, hence easily lost by silence for the virgin.

Source Text

باکرہ کا خیار سکوت سے باطل ہو جاتا ہے، غلام کا خیار رضیت
کہنے سے ختم ہو جاتا ہے
کتاب النکاح
خيار البكر يبطل بالسكوت ولا يبطل خيار الغلام مالم يقل رضيت او يجئى منه ما يعلم انه رضا وکذالک الجارية اذا دخل بها الزوج قبل البلوغ اعتبارا لهذه الحالة بحال ابتداء النكاح وخيار البلوغ في حق البكر لا يمتد الى آخر المجلس ولا يبطل بالقيام فى حق الثيب والغلام لانه ما ثبت باثبات الزوج بل لتوهم الخلل فانما يبطل بالرضاء غير ان سكوت البكر رضا بخلاف خيار العتق لانه ثبت باثبات المولى وهو الاعتاق فيعتبر فيه المجلس كما في خيار المخيرة
ترجمہ پھر خیار بکر باطل ہو جاتا ہے خاموش رہنے سے اور نہیں باطل ہو گا خیار غلام جب تک کہ نہیں کہا رضیت یا نہ آئے اس کی طرف سے وہ چیز کہ جان لیا جائے کہ وہ رضا ہے اور ایسے ہی جاریہ ( شیبہ ) جب دخول کیا اس کے ساتھ شوہر نے بلوغ سے پہلے قیاس کرتے ہوئے اس حالت کو ابتداء نکاح کے حال پر اور خیار بلوغ باکرہ کے حق میں آخر مجلس تک ممتد نہیں ہوگا۔ اور نہیں باطل ہو گا کھڑا ہونے سے شیبہ کے حق میں اور غلام کے حق میں اس لئے کہ خیار بلوغ نہیں ثابت ہوا زوج کے ثابت کرنے سے بلکہ خلل کے وہم کی وجہ سے ۔ چنانچہ خیار بلوغ باطل ہو جاتا ہے رضا مندی سے مگر باکرہ کی خاموشی رضامندی ہے۔ بخلاف خیار عتق کے اس لئے کہ وہ ثابت ہوتا ہے مولیٰ کے ثابت کرنے سے اور وہ حقاق ہے۔ پس اعتبار کیا جائے گا اس میں مجلس کا جیسا کہ خیار مخیرہ میں۔
تشریح اس عبارت میں خیار بلوغ جوند کر اور مؤنث دونوں کو شامل ہے اس پر تفریح ہے تقریر یہ ہوگی کہ باکرہ کا خیار بلور غم سکوت سے باطل ہو جائے گا اور لڑکے کا خیار بلوغ سکوت سے باطل نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ صراحنا رضیت (یعنی میں راضی ہوا) کہے یا کوئی ایسی علامت پائی جائے جو رضامندی پر دلالت کرے۔ مثلاً بالغ ہوتے ہی بیوی کے پاس مہر بھیجدیا یا دوستوں کو دعوتیں کھلانا شروع کر دیں یا بیوی سے جماع کر لیا ان سب چیزوں سے رضا مندی پائی گئی۔ لہذا خیار بلوغ ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح جار یہ شیبہ کہ اس کے ساتھ شوہر نے بالغ ہونے سے پہلے جماع کیا تو اس کے حق میں بھی سکوت کافی نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ صراحتا رضامندی کا اظہار کرے یا کوئی علامت اس کی طرف سے پائی جائے جس سے رضا مندی معلوم ہو سکے۔ مجموعہ کی دلیل ہے کہ اس حالت کو قیاس کیا گیا ہے ابتداء نکاح کی حالت پر قیاس تفصیل یہ ہے کہ صغیرہ باکرہ جب بالغہ ہوگئی اور اس سے ولی نے نکاح کی اجازت مانگی پھر وہ باکرہ بالغہ خاموش رہی تو اس کا یہ سکوت رضا مندی ہوگا ۔ اسی طرح اگر صغیرہ کے لئے خیار بلوغ ہے اور بالغہ ہوگئی اور سکوت اختیار کیا تو اس کا یہ سکوت رضا مندی شمار ہوگا۔ اور خیار باطل ہوگا اس حالت کو ابتداء نکاح کی حالت پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور اسی طرح لڑکا اور جار یہ ثیبہ جب ان سے نکاح کی اجازت مانگی تو ان دونوں کا سکوت رضا مندی نہیں ہوگا بلکہ زبان سے رضا کا اظہار کرے یا کوئی واضح دلالت پائی جائے ۔ یہی حال ہوگا خیار بلوغ کے وقت کہ ان کا سکوت رضا مندی نہیں ہوگا بلکہ زبان سے اظہار کرے یا دلالت و اصحہ پائی جائے اس حالت کو ابتداء نکاح کی حالت پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔ و خيار البلوغ فی حق البکر سے دوسری تفریح ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ خیار بلوغ باکرہ کے حق میں آخر مجلس تک ممتد نہیں ہوگا۔ مجلس سے مراد وہ مجلس ہے جس میں صغیرہ بالغہ ہوئی تھی یعنی جس مجلس میں پہلی مرتبہ خون دیکھا حالانکہ نکاح کی خبر پہلے مل چکی تھی یا بالغہ پہلے ہو چکی تھی اور اب اس مجلس میں نکاح کی خبر ملی تو دونوں صورتوں میں سکوت خیار بلوغ کو باطل کر دیگا۔ اور لڑکے کے حق میں خیار بلوغ کھڑا ہونے سے باطل نہیں ہوگا بلکہ مادر اء مجلس تک ممتد رہے گا۔ خاص طور سے ٹیبہ کے حق میں دلیل یہ ہے کہ ٹیبہ کے لئے خیار بلوغ
The option of the virgin is nullified by silence. The option of the boy is not nullified unless he says 'I consent' or something comes from him that is known to be consent. Similarly, the slave girl (thayyib) if the husband had intercourse with her before puberty, considering this situation like the initial marriage. And the option of puberty for the virgin does not extend to the end of the sitting, and is not nullified by standing up for the thayyib and the boy, because it is not established by the husband's affirmation, but due to the presumption of flaw. So it is nullified by consent, except that the silence of the virgin is consent. Unlike the option of emancipation because it is established by the master's affirmation, which is emancipation, so the sitting is considered as in the option of choice (khiyar al-mukhayyarah).
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage details how khiyar al-bulugh is extinguished for different categories. For a virgin girl, silence itself is considered consent, so her option ends immediately upon silence. For a boy (ghulam) and a thayyib (non-virgin girl), silence is not enough; they must explicitly say 'I consent' or do an act that clearly indicates consent (e.g., sending mahr, having intercourse). The reason given is analogy with the initial marriage contract: when a guardian seeks permission, a virgin's silence is consent, but a thayyib must speak. The same rule applies to khiyar al-bulugh. Additionally, the option for a virgin does not extend beyond the sitting (majlis) in which she attains puberty (or learns of the marriage). If she stands up or leaves, the option is lost. For a thayyib and a boy, standing up does not nullify the option; it remains until they explicitly consent or leave the sitting? The text says it does not become void by standing (la yabtul bil-qiyam). The reasoning: the option is not established by the husband's affirmation but due to the presumption of a defect (tawahhum al-khalal) in the guardian's action, so it is a weak right that is easily extinguished. Contrast with khiyar al-‘itq (option upon emancipation), which is established by the master's act (emancipation), so it requires explicit consent in the sitting, similar to khiyar al-mukhayyarah (option of choice in sales).

Key Terms
بکر (bikr): A virgin girl; in the context of khiyar al-bulugh, her silence is considered consent.
ثیبہ (thayyib): A non-virgin girl; her silence is not consent; she must explicitly consent.
خیار عتق (khiyar al-‘itq): The option of a slave girl to annul her marriage upon being freed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which statement is true about khiyar al-bulugh for a boy?
A) It is nullified by silence immediately upon puberty.
B) It is nullified if he stands up from the sitting.
C) It is nullified only if he says 'I consent' or does a clear act of consent.
D) It is never nullified; he retains the option indefinitely.

Key Takeaway
The extinction of khiyar al-bulugh follows the pattern of the initial marriage contract: a virgin's silence is consent, but a boy or thayyib must explicitly consent.
