If the nearest guardian is absent with an interrupted absence, then it is permissible for someone more distant (than him) to marry her. Zufar said it is not permissible because the guardianship of the nearest remains; it is established as his right to protect the lineage, so it is not invalidated by his absence. For this reason, if he (the nearest) marries her where he is, it is valid, and there is no guardianship for the more distant while the nearest's guardianship exists. Our proof: this guardianship is based on consideration (nazari), and it is not from consideration to entrust to someone whose opinion cannot be utilized. So we entrust it to the more distant, and he is given precedence over the ruler, just as if the nearest had died. If the nearest marries her where he is, there is prohibition (of the more distant's action). After acceptance, we say: the more distant has distance in kinship but closeness in management, and the nearest has the opposite. So they are placed in the position of two equal guardians, and whichever of them contracts (the marriage) it is executed and not rejected. Translation: So when the nearest guardian becomes absent in an interrupted manner, it is permissible for one who is more distant than him to marry her. Imam Zufar said it is not permissible because the guardianship of the nearest exists. Because guardianship is established as a right of the nearest guardian to protect the lineage, so it is not invalidated by his absence. For this reason, if he marries her where he is, it is valid, and there is no guardianship for the more distant.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on marriage guardianship when the nearest guardian (walī aqrab) is absent with an interrupted absence (ghaybah munqaṭiʿah) — meaning his location is unknown and he cannot be contacted. The Hanafi position (the 'we' refers to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) allows the next nearest guardian (walī abʿad) to contract the marriage. Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) opposes this, arguing that the aqrab's right remains valid and is not lost by absence; thus the abʿad cannot act. The Hanafi majority respond with a rational argument: guardianship is a form of consideration (wilāyah nazariyyah), and it is not prudent to entrust marriage decisions to someone whose opinion cannot be obtained. Therefore, the authority transfers to the abʿad, who is preferred over the ruler. They compare this to the case where the aqrab dies — then the abʿad inherits the right. If the aqrab shows up and himself marries her, his marriage is valid and overrides the abʿad's; if both contract separately, they are treated as equal guardians, and the first contract is effective.

Key Terms
غیبة منقطعة (ghaybah munqaṭiʿah): An absence where the person's whereabouts are completely unknown, and there is no way to contact him or know his condition.
ولاية نظرية (wilāyah nazariyyah): Guardianship based on consideration and prudence (nazar), meaning it is given to someone who can exercise best judgment in the ward's interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The next nearest guardian (abʿad) may contract the marriage
D) The marriage is invalid until the aqrab appoints a proxy

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the more distant guardian to contract a marriage when the nearest guardian is absent with interrupted absence, using rational proof (wilāyah nazariyyah) to prioritize the woman's welfare.

Wilayah of Non-Asaba Relatives: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Explaining dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on wilayah in absence of asaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on whether non-asaba relatives have marriage guardianship (wilayah) and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Wilayah is based on compassion, but the mufta bihi restricts it to asaba alone.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary addresses an important intra-Hanafi dispute: when no agnatic relatives (asaba) exist, can other close relatives like a maternal uncle act as marriage guardian? Imam Abu Hanifa, using istihsan (juristic preference), permits it, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) restrict wilayah to asaba only. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi jurists balance textual evidence (the hadith) with rational considerations of compassion (shafaqa).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
State the question: Who has marriage guardianship (wilayah) for a woman when no agnatic relatives (asaba) exist? This is the point of contention.
The issue arises when asaba are absent; the presence of asaba is not disputed.
2
State the Two Hanafi Positions
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that close non-asaba relatives (e.g., maternal uncle, paternal aunt) can be guardians based on istihsan. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that only asaba have wilayah.
Imam Abu Yusuf's view is reported with inconsistency, but the famous (mashhur) position aligns him with Imam Muhammad.
3
Analyze the Proofs
Examine the hadith 'al-nikah ila al-asabaat' and the rational proof (preservation of lineage). The Sahibayn interpret the definite article 'al' as indicating generality, excluding non-asaba. Abu Hanifa restricts the hadith to situations where asaba are present, and argues that wilayah is based on compassion (shafaqa), which non-asaba possess.
Abu Hanifa's use of istihsan overrides the apparent general meaning of the hadith.
4
Understand the Tarjih (Preponderance)
The later Hanafi authorities (e.g., Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah) give preponderance to the Sahibayn's view, making it the mufta bihi (operative ruling). This is because their view is considered more in line with the zahir (apparent) of the hadith and the principle that wilayah preserves lineage.
Despite Abu Hanifa's reasoning, the school adopted the majority opinion of the Sahibayn.
5
Apply the Ruling
According to the mufta bihi, if a marriage is conducted by a non-asaba relative like a maternal uncle without the presence of asaba, the marriage is invalid (batil). The proper guardian would then be the sultan (Imam) or his delegate (qadi).
The text also mentions that the mawla (master who freed a slave) is considered the final asaba.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
كتاب النكاح
کیا اس کا اس کے مولیٰ نے جس نے اس کو آزاد کیا تو جائز ہے اس لئے کہ وہ آخر عصبات ہے۔ اور جب تمام اولیاء ختم ہو جائیں تو ولایت امام اور حاکم کے لئے ہے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فرمان کی وجہ سے یعنی بادشاہ ولی ہے اس شخص کا جسکا کوئی ولی نہیں ۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ عصبات کی عدم موجودگی میں ولایت کس کیلئے ثابت ہوگی۔ اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے امام صاحب کے نزد یک عصبات کے علاوہ دوسرے قرابتداروں کے لئے ثابت ہوگی۔ مثلاً ماموں، خالہ، پھوپی وغیرہ ۔ امام صاحب کا مذہب استحسانا ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک عصبات کے علاوہ دوسرے قرابتداروں کے لئے ولایت ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔ اور قیاس بھی یہی ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف کے قول میں اضطراب ہے۔ لیکن مشہور یہ ہے کہ امام محمد کے ساتھ ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل ماقبل میں روایت کردہ حدیث ہے۔ یعنی النكاح الى العصبات اور الف لام جنس کا ہے تو مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ جنس نکاح سپرد ہے جنس عصبات کے ان کے غیر کو اس میں کوئی دخل نہیں۔ دوسری دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ ولایت قرابت کی حفاظت کیلئے ہے تا کہ قرابت کی طرف غیر کفو کومنسوب کیا جا سکے۔ اور یہ حفاظت ہو گی عصبات کے سپرد کرنے سے۔ اس لئے ولایت کا حق صرف عصبات کو ہے غیر عصبات کو نہیں۔ امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ولایت کا مدار ہے شفقت پر اور شفقت ہر اس شخص میں موجود ہوگی ، جس میں قرابت باعثہ علی الشفقت پائی جائے۔ پس جسمیں ایسی قرابت پائی جائے گی اس کو ولایت حاصل ہوگی عصبہ ہو یا غیر عصبہ اور النكاح الى العصبات حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عصبات کی موجودگی میں نکاح انہی کے سپرد ہو گا۔ لیکن عدم موجودگی میں غیر عصبات کی نفی نہیں کی گئی ۔ صاحب قدوری نے بیان کیا کہ اگر صغیرہ کا ولی نہ ہو یعنی عصبہ نہ ہو بہت قرابت اور اس کا نکاح مولی عناقہ نے کر دیا تو درست ہے کیونکہ وہ آخری عصبہ ہے اور جب کوئی بھی ولی نہ ہو نہ عصبہ نہ غیر عصبہ نہ نبی اور نہ سہی تو اس صورت میں ولایت امام اور حاکم کے لئے ہوگی ۔ امام سے مراد خلیفہ اور حاکم سے مراد اس کا نائب ہے یا حاکم سے مراد قاضی ہے لیکن قاضی کو ولایت نکاح اس وقت حاصل ہوگی جب امام نے اس کو اس کا اختیار دیا ہو۔ دلیل میں حدیث ہے کہ جس کا کوئی ولی نہ ہو اس کا ولی امام ہے۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary Volume 4. Book of Nikah. Whether it is permissible for her master who freed her (to marry her)? Yes, because he is the final asaba. And when all guardians are exhausted, the wilayah belongs to the Imam and the hakim due to the command of the Prophet (peace be upon him) i.e. the king is the guardian of the one who has no guardian. Explanation of the issue: In the absence of asaba, for whom will wilayah be established? There is dispute about this. According to Imam Sahib (Abu Hanifa), it will be established for other relatives besides asaba, e.g., maternal uncle, maternal aunt, paternal aunt, etc. Imam Sahib's madhhab is istihsan. According to Imam Muhammad, wilayah for other relatives besides asaba will not be established, and this is also by qiyas. There is inconsistency in Imam Abu Yusuf's statement, but the famous (position) is that he is with Imam Muhammad. The proof of the two (Sahibayn) is the hadith narrated previously: 'Marriage is for the asaba.' And the lam in 'al-asabaat' is for the genus, so the meaning is that the genus of marriage is entrusted to the genus of asaba; others have no say in it. The second rational proof is that wilayah is for the preservation of lineage, so that lineage is not attributed to a non-kufu. This preservation is achieved by entrusting it to asaba. Therefore, the right of wilayah is only for asaba, not for others. Imam Sahib's proof is that wilayah is based on compassion (shafaqa), and compassion will exist in every person in whom lineage-based compassion is found. So whoever has such lineage will have wilayah, whether asaba or non-asaba. The response to the hadith 'Marriage is for the asaba' is that when asaba are present, marriage is entrusted to them, but in their absence, the negation of non-asaba is not intended. Sahib Quduri stated: If a minor girl has no guardian i.e. no asaba, but has a close relative, and her master (mawla al-'itaq) marries her, it is valid because he is the final asaba. And when there is no guardian at all, neither asaba nor non-asaba, nor prophet nor whatsoever, then in that case wilayah is for the Imam and the hakim. By Imam is meant the Caliph, and by hakim is meant his deputy, or by hakim is meant the qadi, but the qadi will have wilayah for marriage only when the Imam has given him that authority. The evidence is the hadith: 'The one who has no guardian, the Imam is his guardian.'
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage addresses two related issues: first, the case of a freed slave's master who marries her, second, the broader issue of who has the right of marriage guardianship (wilayah) in the absence of asaba (agnatic heirs). The commentary is from the Urdu Sharh of Hidayah, explaining the matn of Quduri. The passage begins by stating that if a master who freed his slave girl marries her, it is valid because he is considered the final asaba (after all other asaba are exhausted). This is a settled ruling. Then it discusses the situation when no asaba exist: the guardianship goes to the Imam (ruler) or his deputy, based on the hadith 'al-sultan wali man la wali lah' (The sultan is guardian of the one who has no guardian). The main dispute in this passage is about non-asaba relatives. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that close non-asaba relatives like maternal uncle, maternal aunt, paternal aunt can be guardians based on istihsan (juristic preference) because guardianship is based on compassion (shafaqa), which these relatives undoubtedly have. His proof is that the hadith 'al-nikah ila al-asabaat' means guardianship is for the asaba when they are present, but does not negate others in their absence. Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf (the Sahibayn) argue that the hadith is general and exclusive: marriage is entrusted only to asaba, using the grammatical point that the definite article 'al' indicates genus, thus excluding non-asaba. They also provide a rational proof: guardianship preserves lineage, and this is best achieved by asaba who inherit. The commentary notes that the famous (mashhur) position is that of Imam Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf's view is unsettled but ultimately agrees with him. Thus the mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that only asaba have wilayah; non-asaba do not. The text also includes a quote from Quduri's matn: if a minor girl has no asaba, her master (mawla al-'itaq) can marry her because he is the last asaba. This is consistent with the asaba-only view. If even the mawla is absent, then the Imam or his delegate (qadi) assumes guardianship. This passage highlights an important intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and the method of istinbat (deduction) from hadith and rational considerations.

Key Terms
عصبات (ʿaṣabāt): Agnatic relatives (male line) who inherit as residuaries or are entitled to guardianship in marriage.
ولایت (wilāyah): The legal authority to contract a marriage on behalf of another, especially a minor or insane person.
استحسان (istiḥsān): A method of legal reasoning where a ruling is preferred due to equity or public interest over a strict analogy (qiyas).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Her maternal uncle
B) The Imam or his delegate (qadi)
C) Her paternal aunt
D) No one; she must marry herself

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that only asaba (agnatic relatives) have marriage guardianship; in their absence, it transfers to the sultan or his delegate.

Ghayba Muntaqita: When the Nearest Wali is Unreachable
Explaining when the distant wali may act in place of the absent nearest wali

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ghayba muntaqita, explain the reasoning of Imam Zufar, and apply the school's tarjih to determine who may act as guardian.

Core Idea
The distant wali (ab'ad) takes precedence over the ruler when the nearest wali is absent with interrupted absence.

In Hanafi marriage law, the sequence of guardians (wilaayat tazwīj) is fixed by lineage. But what happens when the nearest wali (e.g., father) is alive but unreachable—no one knows his whereabouts or cannot communicate with him? This is called ghayba muntaqita (interrupted absence). The Hanafi school faces an internal dispute: does the distant wali (ab'ad) step in, or must the woman wait indefinitely? This lesson unpacks the reasoning from Al-Hidayah and the critical difference with Imam Zufar.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
From the matn: when the nearest wali is absent with ghayba muntaqita, the more distant wali (ab'ad) has the authority to contract the marriage. He is even preferred over the sultan.
This is the relied-upon position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) holds that the ab'ad cannot act because the nearest wali's wilaayah remains intact as a right to preserve lineage.
Zufar's view is a minority position within the Hanafi school.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Zufar argues that if the nearest wali married her from a distance (even while absent), it would be valid. This proves his wilaayah continues, thus excluding the ab'ad.
The proof relies on the premise that absence does not nullify a right.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The majority responds two ways: (a) the nearest wali's marriage in absence is invalid, or (b) if it is valid, it is because both are like equal guardians—whoever acts first wins. The ab'ad is not excluded.
The key principle: wilaayah is based on consideration (nazari) and the ward's best interest.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: If a girl's father is missing with no contact, the grandfather can marry her according to the Hanafi majority; Zufar would require waiting for the father. The tarjih favours the majority.
This prevents hardship for the woman.

Source Text

ولی اثرب غیبت منقطعہ پر ہو تو ولی ابعد کیلئے ولایت ہے
فاد غاب الولى الاقرب غيبة منقطعة جاز لمن هو ابعد منه ان يزوج وقال زفر لا يجوزلان ولاية الاقرب قائمة لأنها تثبت حقاله صيانة للقرابة فلاتبطل بغيبته ولهذا لوزوجها حيث هو جاز ولا ولاية للابعد مع ولايته ولنا ان هذه ولاية نظرية وليس من النظر التفويض الى من لا ينتفع برايه ففوضناه الى الابعد وهو مقدم على السلطان كما اذامات الاقرب ولوزوجها حيث هو فيه منع وبعد التسليم نقول للابعد بعد القرابة وقرب التدبير وللاقرب عكسه فنزلا منزلته وليين متساويين فايهما عقد نفذولايرد
ترجمہ ۔ پس جب ولی اقرب غائب ہو گیا غیبت منقطعہ کے طور پر تو اس کے لئے جائز ہے جو اس سے ابعد ہو یہ کہ نکاح کرے۔ اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ جائز نہیں۔ اس لئے کہ اقرب کی ولایت موجود ہے۔ اسلئے کہ ولایت ثابت ہوئی ولی اقرب کا حق بن کر قرابت کو محفوظ کرنے کیلئے ۔ پس نہیں باطل ہوگی اس کی غیبت اور اسی وجہ سے اگر نکاح کر دیا اس کا جہاں ہو وہ تو جائز ہے اور ابعد کیلئے ولایت نہیں ہوتی اقرب کی موجودگی میں اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ولایت نظری ہے۔ اور کوئی شفقت نہیں نکاح کو سپرد کرنا اس شخص کی طرف جسکی رائے سے نفع نہیں اٹھایا جاسکتا ہے۔ لہذا ہم نے اس کو ولی ابعد کے سپرد کر دیا اور ولی ابعد مقدم ہے حاکم اور امام پر جیسا کہ جب ولی اقرب مر گیا اور اگر نکاح کیا اس کا جہاں وہ موجود ہو تو اس میں منع ہے اور تسلیم کر لینے کے بعد ہم جواب دیں گے کہ ولی ابعد کے لئے بعد قرابت اور قرب تدبیر ہے اور ولی اقرب کے لئے قرب قرابت اور بعد تدبیر ہے۔ پس اتار لیا جائے گا دونوں کو دو برابر کے درجہ کے ولیوں کے مرتبہ میں پس ان دونوں میں سے جس نے بھی نکاح کیا وہ نافذ کیا جائے گا اور رد نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح ماقبل میں صاحب ہدایہ نے بیان فرمایا تھا کہ ولی ابعد محروم ہو گا ولی اقرب کی موجودگی میں اس پر یہ مسئلہ متفرع ہے۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ولی اقرب مثلاً باپ غیبت منقطعہ کے طور پر غائب ہو گیا تو ولی ابعد مثلاً دادا کے لئے ولایت تزویج ثابت ہوگی یا نہیں یعنی ولی اقرب کی عدم موجودگی میں ولی البعد نکاح کرنے کا مجاز ہوگایا نہیں ہمارے نزدیک تو جائز ہے اور امام زفر نا جائز کہتے ہیں۔ امام زفر کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ولی اقرب کی ولایت موجود ہے کیوں کہ وہ اس کے لئے حق بنکر ثابت ہوئی ہے تاکہ قرابت کی حفاظت کر سکے ۔ لہذا ولی اقرب کے غائب ہو جانے سے اس کی ولایت باطل نہیں ہوگی۔ اور اس کی تائید اس سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ ولی اقرب نے اگر صغیرہ کا نکاح وہیں رہتے ہوئے کر دیا جہاں وہ سفر میں موجود تھا تو یہ نکاح شرعاً درست ہے۔ اس سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ولی اقرب کی ولایت باقی ہے ورنہ اس کا کیا ہوا نکاح درست نہ ہوتا اور جب ولی اقرب کی ولایت باقی ہے تو ولی البعد کوحق ولایت حاصل نہیں ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ ولی اقرب کی ولایت کے باقی رہتے ہوئے ولی البعد محروم رہتا ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ولایت کامدار شفقت پر ہے اور جس شخص کی رائے سے نفع اٹھا ناممکن نہ ہو تو امور نکاح اس کے سپرد کرنے میں کوئی شفقت نہیں ہے اس لئے ہم نے نکاح ولی ابعد کے سپرد کر دیا اور ولی ابعد ہمارے نزدیک امام اور حاکم پر مقدم ہے جیسا کہ جب ولی اقرب مر جائے ۔ وهـو مـقـدم على السلطان میں امام شافعی پر رد ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر ولی اقرب مر جائے تو ولایت ولی ابعد کی طرف منتقل نہیں ہوگی بلکہ امام وقت کی طرف منتقل ہو گی اسی طرح اگر ولی اقرب غائب ہو جائے تب بھی ان کے نزدیک امام وقت کو ولایت حاصل ہوگی ولی ابعد کو نہیں لیکن ہمارے نزدیک ولی ابعد امام وقت پر مقدم ہے۔ حضرت امام زفر کے قول و لوزوجها حيث ھو کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ہم اسکو تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ ولی اقرب جہاں بھی موجود ہو وہیں رہتے ہوئے اگر نکاح کر دیا تو درست ہو گا بلکہ ہماری رائے یہ ہے کہ نکاح درست نہیں ہوگا۔ لہذا اس مسئلہ کو دلیل میں پیش کرنا مناست نہیں ہے اور اگر ہم تسلیم بھی کر لیں کہ ولی اقرب کا بحالت غیبت کیا ہوا نکاح درست ہو گیا تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ولی اقرب اور ولی ابعد دونوں میں ایک خوبی اور ایک ایک خرابی ہے کیونکہ ولی ابعد میں بُعد قرابت اور قرب تدبیر ہے۔ اور ولی اقرب میں قرب قرابت اور بعد تدبیر ہے۔ پس یہ دونوں ایسے ہو گئے جیسا کہ ایک درجہ کے دو ولی ہوں، اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ اگر برابر درجہ کے دو ولی ہوں تو ان دونوں میں سے جو بھی عقد نکاح کر دے گا وہ نافذ ہو گا اس کو رد نہیں کیا جا سکتا اسی طرح یہاں بھی جو عقد کرے گا وہ نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے ولی اقرب کا کیا ہوا نکاح نافذ ہو گیا ہے۔
The rule: When the nearest wali is absent with interrupted absence, the more distant wali has wilaayah. So if the nearest wali is absent with interrupted absence, it is permissible for one more distant than him to marry (her). Zufar said: Not permissible because the wilaayah of the nearest is established, as it is established as his right for the preservation of lineage, so it does not become void by his absence. Hence, if he marries her where he is, it is valid, and there is no wilaayah for the more distant while his wilaayah exists. Our proof is that this wilaayah is based on consideration (nazari), and it is not a matter of consideration to delegate to one whose opinion cannot be beneficial. So we have delegated it to the more distant, and he is given precedence over the sultan, just as when the nearer dies. If he marries her where he is, there is objection. After submission, we say: The more distant has distant lineage but close planning (qubb al-tadbeer), while the nearer has close lineage but distant planning. So they are treated as two equal guardians: whichever one conducts the marriage, it is effective and not rejected. Translation: So when the nearest wali is absent with interrupted absence, it is permissible for the more distant to marry her. Imam Zufar said: Not permissible, because the wilaayah of the nearest is existing, as it was established as his right to preserve lineage, so it does not become void by his absence. For this reason, if he marries her where he is, it is valid, and there is no wilaayah for the more distant in the presence of his wilaayah. Our proof is that this wilaayah is based on consideration, and there is no compassion in entrusting marriage to one whose opinion cannot be utilized. Therefore we have entrusted it to the more distant, and the more distant is given precedence over the sultan, just as when the nearest dies. If he marries her where he is, it is prohibited. After submission, we respond that the more distant has distant lineage but close planning, and the nearer has close lineage but distant planning. So they are treated like two equal-ranking guardians: whichever one conducts the marriage, it is effective and not rejected. Explanation: In the previous text, Sahib al-Hidayah stated that the more distant wali is excluded when the nearer wali is present. This issue is derived from that. The issue is: if the nearest wali, e.g., father, is absent with interrupted absence, will wilaayah for marriage be established for the more distant wali, e.g., grandfather? i.e., in the absence of the nearest wali, is the more distant authorized to marry? According to us, it is permissible; Imam Zufar says it is not permissible. The gist of Imam Zufar's proof: The nearest wali's wilaayah exists because it was established as a right for him to preserve lineage, so it does not become void by his absence. This is supported by the fact that if the nearest wali marries the minor girl while he is in his travel, it is valid. This shows that his wilaayah remains; otherwise, his marriage would not be valid. When his wilaayah remains, the more distant has no right because he is excluded. Our proof: Wilaayah is based on compassion, and there is no compassion in entrusting marriage to one whose opinion cannot be utilized. Therefore we have entrusted it to the more distant. And the more distant is preferred over the Imam and the hakim, just as when the nearest dies. 'Wa huwa muqaddam 'ala al-sultan' is a refutation of Imam Shafi'i, because he says that if the nearest wali dies, wilaayah does not transfer to the more distant but to the ruler. Similarly, if the nearest is absent, according to him, the ruler has wilaayah, not the more distant. But according to us, the more distant is preferred over the ruler. The response to Imam Zufar's statement 'law zawwajaha haythu huwa' is that we do not accept that if the nearest wali marries her while he is there (in the far place), it is valid. Rather, our opinion is that it is not valid, so using this issue as proof is inappropriate. If we do concede that the nearest wali's marriage in absence is valid, the reason is that both the nearer and more distant have one good and one bad quality: the more distant has distance in lineage but closeness in planning, while the nearer has closeness in lineage but distance in planning. Thus they become like two equal guardians, and the rule is that if there are two equal guardians, whichever one conducts the marriage, it is effective and cannot be rejected. So the marriage conducted by the nearest wali is effective.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage from the Urdu commentary on Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: when a woman's nearest marriage guardian (wali aqrab) is absent in a way that contact is impossible (ghayba muntaqita), can the next closest guardian (wali ab'ad) step in? The matn from Hidayah states it is permissible for the ab'ad to marry her, and this is the Hanafi position. Imam Zufar, a Hanafi scholar who often differed, disagrees, arguing that the aqrab's wilaayah remains intact as a right to preserve lineage, and if the aqrab married her from afar, it would be valid. Thus the ab'ad has no right. The Hanafi response is twofold. First, they argue that wilaayah is based on 'nazari' (looking after interests) and compassion (shafaqa). It would not be in her interest to defer to someone whose opinion cannot be sought or implemented. Therefore, the ab'ad is preferred, and his authority is even given precedence over the sultan (ruler). This is analogous to the case of the aqrab's death. Second, regarding Zufar's claim that the aqrab's marriage in absentia would be valid, the Hanafis either reject that premise outright (saying it would not be valid) or, if accepted, they explain that the aqrab and ab'ad are like two equal-ranking guardians, each with advantages (aqrab: close lineage but far in planning; ab'ad: far lineage but close in planning). The rule for equal guardians is that whichever one conducts the marriage first, it is effective. Thus the aqrab's marriage being valid does not negate the ab'ad's right; rather, it is a race. The passage also refutes Imam Shafi'i's view that upon the aqrab's death, wilaayah goes to the sultan rather than the ab'ad. The Hanafi school firmly holds that the ab'ad is preferred over the sultan in both absence and death. This lesson demonstrates how Hanafi scholars preserved flexibility in guardianship to avoid leaving women without a guardian.

Key Terms
غیبت منقطعة (ghaybah munqaṭiʿah): An absence where the wali is alive but his whereabouts are unknown or communication is impossible, effectively cutting off his ability to act.
ولایت نظری (wilāyah naẓariyyah): A type of guardianship based on consideration of the ward's best interests, not merely a personal right.
ولایت تزویج (wilāyat tazwīj): The authority to contract a marriage on behalf of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of ghayba muntaqita (interrupted absence) of the father, who does the Hanafi school hold as the preferred guardian to marry the daughter?
A) The qadi (judge)
B) The next closest relative (e.g., grandfather)
C) The mother
D) The daughter herself if she is of age

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves the issue of an unreachable nearest wali by empowering the next closest guardian, prioritising the ward's welfare over rigid adherence to rank.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Authority of the Distant Guardian During Disconnected Absence
Intra-Hanafi dispute on guardian authority during disconnected absence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the distant guardian's authority during the close guardian's disconnected absence and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar, including the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
When the closest guardian is unreachable, affection demands entrusting marriage to the next closest, not the ruler.

This lesson examines a classic fiqh scenario: the close guardian (e.g., father) is absent in a way that makes communication impossible. Who then has the right to give the minor in marriage? The Hanafi school gives this authority to the distant guardian (e.g., grandfather), while Imam Zufar maintains the close guardian's authority persists. We will unpack the proofs and the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Read the first few lines to see the two positions: according to us (Hanafis) it is permissible, Imam Zufar says not permissible.
Label the two sides clearly.
2
Analyze Zufar's proof
Zufar argues that the close guardian's authority is a right that does not vanish with absence; he supports this with the validity of a marriage contracted by the close guardian while away.
Look for the phrase 'و لوزوجها حيث هو'.
3
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response bases authority on affection (shafaqah). If the close guardian's opinion cannot be obtained timely, there is no benefit in retaining his authority, so it transfers to the distant guardian.
Note the priority given to the distant guardian over the ruler.
4
Consider the counter-argument about validity of close guardian's marriage
The Hanafis either deny that such a marriage is valid, or if accepted, explain it by equating the two guardians as equal in merit and deficiency, making both marriages effective.
This is a nuanced legal reasoning using the principle of equal guardians.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The majority Hanafi position (three imams) is relied upon. Practically, the distant guardian can marry the ward, whereas in Zufar's view he cannot, and in Shafi'i's view only the ruler can.
This difference affects real-life marriage arrangements.

مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ولی اقرب مثلاً باپ غیبت منقطعہ کے طور پر غائب ہو گیا تو ولی ابعد مثلاً دادا کے لئے ولایت تزویج ثابت ہوگی یا نہیں یعنی ولی اقرب کی عدم موجودگی میں ولی البعد نکاح کرنے کا مجاز ہوگا یا نہیں ہمارے نزدیک تو جائز ہے اور امام زفر نا جائز کہتے ہیں۔ امام زفر کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ولی اقرب کی ولایت موجود ہے کیوں کہ وہ اس کے لئے حق بنکر ثابت ہوئی ہے تاکہ قرابت کی حفاظت کر سکے۔ لہذا ولی اقرب کے غائب ہو جانے سے اس کی ولایت باطل نہیں ہوگی۔ اور اس کی تائید اس سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ ولی اقرب نے اگر صغیرہ کا نکاح وہیں رہتے ہوئے کر دیا جہاں وہ سفر میں موجود تھا تو یہ نکاح شرعاً درست ہے۔ اس سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ولی اقرب کی ولایت باقی ہے ورنہ اس کا کیا ہوا نکاح درست نہ ہوتا اور جب ولی اقرب کی ولایت باقی ہے تو ولی البعد کو حق ولایت حاصل نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ولی اقرب کی ولایت کے باقی رہتے ہوئے ولی البعد محروم رہتا ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ولایت کا مدار شفقت پر ہے اور جس شخص کی رائے سے نفع اٹھانا ممکن نہ ہو تو امور نکاح اس کے سپرد کرنے میں کوئی شفقت نہیں ہے اس لئے ہم نے نکاح ولی ابعد کے سپرد کر دیا اور ولی ابعد ہمارے نزدیک امام اور حاکم پر مقدم ہے جیسا کہ جب ولی اقرب مر جائے۔ وهومقدم على السلطان میں امام شافعی پر رد ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر ولی اقرب مر جائے تو ولایت ولی ابعد کی طرف منتقل نہیں ہوگی بلکہ امام وقت کی طرف منتقل ہو گی اسی طرح اگر ولی اقرب غائب ہو جائے تب بھی ان کے نزدیک امام وقت کو ولایت حاصل ہوگی ولی ابعد کو نہیں لیکن ہمارے نزدیک ولی ابعد امام وقت پر مقدم ہے۔ حضرت امام زفر کے قول و لوزوجها حيث هو کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ہم اس کو تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ ولی اقرب جہاں بھی موجود ہو وہیں رہتے ہوئے اگر نکاح کر دیا تو درست ہوگا بلکہ ہماری رائے یہ ہے کہ نکاح درست نہیں ہوگا۔ لہذا اس مسئلہ کو دلیل میں پیش کرنا مناست نہیں ہے اور اگر ہم تسلیم بھی کر لیں کہ ولی اقرب کا بحالت غیبت کیا ہوا نکاح درست ہو گیا تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ولی اقرب اور ولی ابعد دونوں میں ایک خوبی اور ایک ایک خرابی ہے کیونکہ ولی ابعد میں بعد قرابت اور قرب تدبیر ہے۔ اور ولی اقرب میں قرب قرابت اور بعد تدبیر ہے۔ پس یہ دونوں ایسے ہو گئے جیسا کہ ایک درجہ کے دو ولی ہوں، اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ اگر برابر درجہ کے دو ولی ہوں تو ان دونوں میں سے جو بھی عقد نکاح کر دے گا وہ نافذ ہو گا اس کو رد نہیں کیا جا سکتا اسی طرح یہاں بھی جو عقد کرے گا وہ نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے ولی اقرب کا کیا ہوا نکاح نافذ ہو گیا ہے۔
The issue is: When the close guardian, e.g., father, is absent in a disconnected absence, does the distant guardian, e.g., grandfather, have the authority of marriage? That is, in the absence of the close guardian, is the distant guardian permitted to contract marriage? According to us, it is permissible, and Imam Zufar says it is not permissible. The summary of Imam Zufar's proof is that the authority of the close guardian exists because it is established for him as a right to protect kinship. Therefore, his authority does not become invalid due to his absence. This is also supported by the fact that if the close guardian contracts the marriage of a minor girl while staying in the place where he was present during travel, that marriage is valid in Shariah. This also indicates that the close guardian's authority remains; otherwise, his marriage would not be valid. And when the close guardian's authority remains, the distant guardian does not acquire the right of authority, because the distant guardian is deprived as long as the close guardian's authority remains. Our proof is that the basis of authority is affection (shafaqah), and when it is not possible to benefit from the opinion of a person, there is no affection in entrusting marriage matters to him. Therefore, we entrust the marriage to the distant guardian. And according to us, the distant guardian is given priority over the ruler and the judge, just as when the close guardian dies. 'And it is given precedence over the sultan' is a refutation of Imam Shafi'i because he says that if the close guardian dies, authority does not transfer to the distant guardian but to the time's ruler. Similarly, if the close guardian is absent, according to him, the ruler acquires authority, not the distant guardian. But according to us, the distant guardian is given precedence over the time's ruler. The answer to Imam Zufar's statement 'and if he marries her where he is' is that we do not accept that if the close guardian, wherever he may be, contracts marriage while staying there, it is valid. Rather, our opinion is that the marriage is not valid. Therefore, presenting this issue as evidence is not appropriate. And if we even accept that the marriage contracted by the close guardian during absence is valid, its reason is that both the close and distant guardians have one good quality and one deficiency each. Because the distant guardian has distant kinship but near planning, and the close guardian has near kinship but distant planning. So both become like two guardians of the same rank. And the rule is that if there are two guardians of equal rank, whichever of them contracts the marriage, it will be effective and cannot be rejected. Similarly, here whichever contracts the marriage, it will be effective. Therefore, the marriage contracted by the close guardian is effective.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the authority of the distant guardian (wali ab'ad) when the close guardian (wali aqrab) is absent with a disconnected absence (ghaybat munqati'ah). The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) holds that the distant guardian has authority, while Imam Zufar disagrees, arguing that the close guardian's authority remains valid during absence, as evidenced by the validity of his marriage contract if he performs it while away. The commentator then provides the Hanafi response: the basis of authority is affection (shafaqah), and since the close guardian's opinion cannot be sought in a timely manner, entrusting the marriage to him would not serve the ward's interest. Therefore, the distant guardian is preferred, and he takes precedence even over the ruler. The objection that the close guardian's marriage is valid is addressed by either denying its validity or, if accepted, equating the close and distant guardians to two equal guardians whose contracts are both valid. The passage also references Imam Shafi'i's position that authority transfers to the ruler, not the distant guardian, and refutes it.

Key Terms
ولی اقرب (walī aqrab): The nearest male guardian (e.g., father) with a strong kinship tie and authority over marriage.
ولی ابعد (walī ab'ad): A more distant male guardian (e.g., grandfather) who assumes authority when the close guardian is absent or incapacitated.
غیبت منقطعہ (ghayba munqaṭi'a): A disconnected absence where the guardian is in a place that cannot be reached by caravans within a year or similar condition, making communication impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who has the authority to marry a minor girl when her father is absent in a disconnected absence (ghaybat munqati'ah)?
A) The distant guardian (e.g., grandfather) takes precedence over the ruler.
B) The ruler (sultan) has the exclusive authority.
C) The father's authority remains, so no one else can marry her.
D) The mother can marry her.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when the close guardian is unreachable (disconnected absence), the distant guardian assumes authority over marriage, taking precedence even over the ruler.

beginner

Three Definitions of Disconnected Absence (Ghaybat Munqati'ah)
Definition of disconnected absence with three scholarly views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three definitions of ghaybat munqati'ah and identify which is preferred in Hanafi fiqh based on the rationale of affection.

Core Idea
The ruling definition of disconnected absence is when waiting for the guardian would lose a compatible match.

In Hanafi marriage law, a distant guardian's authority to act depends on whether his absence is 'disconnected' (ghaybat munqati'ah). Scholars offered three criteria, each rooted in a different understanding of when the guardian's permission becomes impractical. This lesson examines each view and why the third is closest to the spirit of the law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first definition: al-Quduri's view
Imam al-Quduri defined disconnected absence as being in a city where caravans arrive only once a year. This is a fixed temporal criterion.
This view relies on customary travel patterns.
2
Identify the second definition: minimum travel distance
Some later scholars said it is the minimum distance that makes travel permissible (three days' journey), since there is no maximum.
This view focuses on the guardian's inability to return quickly.
3
Identify the third and preferred definition: risk of losing kufu'
The leading view is that disconnected absence occurs when seeking the guardian's opinion would cause the loss of a suitable match (kufu'). This is called 'closest to fiqh' because it directly serves the ward's interest (shafaqah).
This definition prioritizes the purpose of guardianship over fixed time/distance limits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والغيبة المنقطعة ان يكون فى بلد لاتصل اليه القوافل فى السنة الامرة وهو اختيار القدورى وقيل أدنى مدة السفر لانه لانهاية لاقصاه وهو اختيار بعض المتاخرين وقيل اذا كان بحال يفوت الكفوباستطلاع رايه وهذا اقرب الى الفقه لانه لانظر في ابقاء ولايته حينئذ. ترجمه: غیبت منقطعہ یہ ہے کہ ایسے شہر میں ہو کہ نہ پہنچے قافلہ اس کی طرف سال میں مگر ایک مرتبہ اور یہ قدوری کا پسندیدہ (قول ہے) اور کہا گیا کہ ادنی مدت سفر اس لئے کہ منتہی سفر کی کوئی انتہا نہیں ہے اور یہ قول بعض متأخرین کا پسند کردہ ہے اور کہا گیا کہ جب ایسے حال میں ہو کہ کفو فوت ہو جائے اس کی رائے پر اطلاع پانے سے اور یہ قول اقرب الی الفقہ ہے۔ اس لئے وقت ولایت کو باقی رکھنے میں کوئی شفقت نہیں۔
And disconnected absence (ghaybat munqati'ah) is that he be in a city where caravans do not reach it except once a year. This is the choice of al-Quduri. And it was said: the minimum duration of travel, because there is no limit to its maximum, and this is the choice of some later scholars. And it was said: when it is in such a state that the kufu' (compatibility) would be lost due to seeking his opinion, and this is closest to fiqh because there is no consideration in preserving his authority then. Translation: Disconnected absence is that he is in a city where the caravan does not reach it except once a year, and this is the preferred statement of al-Quduri. And it was said: the minimum duration of travel, because the maximum of travel has no limit, and this is the statement preferred by some later scholars. And it was said: when it is such a state that the kufu' would be lost by obtaining his opinion, and this statement is closest to fiqh. Because there is no affection in preserving his authority at that time.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'ghaybat munqati'ah' (disconnected absence), a key condition for the distant guardian's authority. Al-Quduri defines it as being in a place where caravans arrive only once a year. Some later scholars say it is any journey of at least three days (minimum travel distance), since there is no maximum. The third view, attributed to scholars like Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, is that it occurs when waiting for the guardian's opinion would cause the loss of a suitable match (kufu'). The author notes this view is closest to fiqh because it directly relates to the purpose of guardianship: affection (shafaqah) for the ward's interest. If the kufu' would be lost, preserving the guardian's authority serves no affection. This definition determines when the distant guardian may act.

Key Terms
غیبت منقطعہ (ghayba munqaṭi'a): A state where the guardian is absent and cannot be contacted in time for marriage decisions, defined by three possible criteria: yearly caravan access, minimum travel distance, or risk of losing a suitable match.
کفو (kufu'): Compatibility between the spouses in terms of lineage, religion, profession, etc., a condition for a valid marriage in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which definition of ghaybat munqati'ah is considered closest to fiqh according to the text?
A) Being in a city where caravans come once a year.
B) Being away for at least the minimum travel distance (three days).
C) When obtaining the guardian's opinion would cause the loss of a suitable match (kufu').
D) Being absent for more than one year.

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi definition of disconnected absence is functional: it exists when waiting for the guardian would lose a compatible match.

Guardian of a Mentally Incompetent Woman: Father vs. Son
Dispute on whether the father or adult son has guardianship over a mentally incompetent woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the guardianship of a mentally incompetent woman when both father and adult son are present, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the basis of guardianship.

Core Idea
Guardianship is based on 'asabah, not affection; the son precedes the father.

When a mentally incompetent woman (majnunah) has both a living father and an adult son, a question arises: who has the right to be her marriage guardian? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement. The two shaykhs, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, hold that the son is the guardian because guardianship follows 'asabah (agnatic priority). Imam Muhammad, however, argues that the father's greater affection makes him more suitable. This lesson examines both proofs and identifies the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Sahibayn)
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the son is the guardian. Note their reasoning: 'asabah is the basis of guardianship, and the son is closer in 'asabah than the father.
The mufta bihi follows this view.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Recognize that Imam Muhammad holds the father is the guardian. His proof: the father has more affection (shafaqah) than the son.
Affection is a valid consideration in some rulings.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The two shaykhs respond that increased affection is not considered, just as the maternal grandfather is not given precedence over 'asabat despite possibly having more affection.
Consistency in applying 'asabah as the criterion.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the son contracts the marriage, it is valid; if the father does so without the son's presence, the marriage may be disputed.
In practice, the son's consent is necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اجتمع فى المجنونة ابوها وابنها فالولّى فى انكاحها ابنها فى قول أبي حنيفة وابي يوسف وقال محمد ابوها لانه اوفر شفقة من الابن ولهما ان الابن هو المقدم فى العصوبة وهذه الولاية مبنية عليها ولا معتبر بزيادة الشفقة كاب الام مع بعض العصبات والله اعلم. ترجمه: اور جب جمع ہو جائیں مجنونہ عورت میں اس کا باپ اور اس کا بیٹا تو اس کا نکاح کرنے میں اس کا ولی اقرب اس کا بیٹا ہے شیخین کے قول کے مطابق۔ اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ اس کا باپ ہے اس لئے کہ باپ بیٹے کے مقابلہ میں زیادہ شفقت رکھتا ہے۔ اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیٹا عصبہ ہونے میں مقدم ہے۔ اور یہ ولایت اسی عصوبت پر مبنی ہے اور زیادتی شفقت کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا جیسا کہ ماں کا باپ یعنی نانا بعض عصبات کے ساتھ۔
And when the father and her son are present for a mentally incompetent woman (majnunah), then the guardian in her marriage is her son according to the statement of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: her father, because he has more affection (shafaqah) than the son. And for them (the two shaykhs) is that the son is given precedence in 'asabah (residuaries), and this authority (wilayah) is built upon it, and increase in affection is not considered, just like the maternal grandfather with some 'asabat (agnatic heirs). And Allah knows best. Translation: And when the father and her son are both present for a mentally incompetent woman, then the guardian of her marriage is her son according to the two shaykhs. And Imam Muhammad said: her father, because the father has more affection than the son. And the proof of the two shaykhs is that the son is given precedence in 'asabah, and this authority is based on that, and an increase in affection is not considered, just like the maternal grandfather with some 'asabat.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the guardian for a mentally incompetent woman (majnunah) when both her father and her adult son are alive. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) hold that the son is the guardian and therefore has the right to contract her marriage. Their reasoning: guardianship (wilayat al-tazwij) is based on 'asabah (agnatic relations), and in the order of 'asabah, the son is closer than the father. Increased affection (shafaqah) is not considered, just as the maternal grandfather is not given precedence over closer 'asabat despite possibly having more affection. Imam Muhammad argues that the father should be the guardian because he has more affection for his daughter than her son, and affection is the basis of guardianship. The commentator indicates that the view of the two shaykhs is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
مجنونہ (majnūna): A mentally incompetent woman who lacks legal capacity and requires a guardian for marriage.
عصوبت (‘uṣūba): Agnatic relationship, the basis for inheritance and guardianship rights for males through the male line.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, who is the guardian for a mentally incompetent woman (majnunah) when both her father and adult son are present?
A) The father, because of greater affection.
B) The son, because of priority in 'asabah.
C) The ruler, because both are absent.
D) The mother, as a close relative.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, guardianship for marriage is based on 'asabah, so the son precedes the father as guardian for a mentally incompetent woman.
